2:27:1588:0:14:72:454:700:12:Times:12:Times:C:A Walrasian Theory of Sovereign Debt Auctions with Asymmetric Information
2:28:1661:14:14:72:335:686:12:Times:12:Times:C:Harold Cole, Daniel Neuhann, and Guillermo Ordoñez
2:29:1711:14:14:72:234:672:12:Times:12:Times:C:NBER Working Paper No. 24890
2:30:1739:14:14:72:134:658:12:Times:12:Times:C:August 2018
2:31:1750:14:28:72:231:644:12:Times:12:Times:C:JEL No. D4,D44,D53,E4,E5,F34
2:32:1778:28:28:273:338:616:12:Times:12:Times:C:ABSTRACT
2:33:1786:28:14:72:546:588:12:Times:12:Times:C:How   does   investors'   information   about   a   country's   fundamentals,   and   the   fact   that   this 
2:34:1897:14:14:72:545:574:12:Times:12:Times:C:information may  be  asymmetrically  held,  affect  a  country's  financing  cost?  Motivated  by  this 
2:35:2000:14:14:72:546:560:12:Times:12:Times:C:question, and by the observation that sovereign bonds are usually auctioned in large lots to a large 
2:36:2100:14:14:72:546:546:12:Times:12:Times:C:number   of   potential investors,   we   develop   a   novel   model   of   auctions   with   asymmetric 
2:37:2205:14:14:71:546:532:12:Times:12:Times:C:information that relies on price-taking and rational expectations. We first characterize sovereign 
2:38:2303:14:14:72:545:518:12:Times:12:Times:C:bond prices for different degrees of asymmetric information under two commonly-used protocols: 
2:39:2397:14:14:72:545:504:12:Times:12:Times:C:discriminatory-price  auctions  and  uniform-price auctions.  We  show  that  there  is  trade-off 
2:40:2495:14:14:72:546:490:12:Times:12:Times:C:between  these  protocols  if  information  is  sufficiently  asymmetric: expected  bond  yields  are 
2:41:2596:14:14:72:545:476:12:Times:12:Times:C:higher when pricing is discriminatory, but yield volatility is higher when pricing is uniform.  We 
2:42:2694:14:14:72:545:462:12:Times:12:Times:C:then  study  endogenous  information  acquisition  and  find  that  (i)  discriminatory auctions  may 
2:43:2795:14:14:72:545:448:12:Times:12:Times:C:display  multiple  welfare-ranked  informational  equilibria,  and  (ii)  investors  are  less  likely to 
2:44:2900:14:28:72:267:434:12:Times:12:Times:C:acquire information in uniform auctions.
2:45:2940:28:14:72:131:406:12:Times:12:Times:C:Harold Cole
2:46:2951:14:14:72:185:392:12:Times:12:Times:C:Economics Department
2:47:2971:14:14:72:203:378:12:Times:12:Times:C:University of Pennsylvania
2:48:2997:14:14:72:161:364:12:Times:12:Times:C:3718 Locust Walk
2:49:3013:14:14:72:175:350:12:Times:12:Times:C:160 McNeil Building

2:53:3082:28:14:72:150:280:12:Times:12:Times:C:Daniel Neuhann
2:54:3096:14:14:72:240:266:12:Times:12:Times:C:Department of Finance CBA 6.278
2:55:3127:14:14:72:217:252:12:Times:12:Times:C:McCombs School of Business

2:62:3293:14:14:306:409:364:12:Times:12:Times:C:428 McNeil Building
2:63:3312:14:14:306:395:350:12:Times:12:Times:C:3718 Locust Walk
2:64:3328:14:14:306:420:336:12:Times:12:Times:C:Philadelphia, PA 19104
2:65:3350:14:14:306:358:322:12:Times:12:Times:C:and NBER
2:66:3358:14:0:306:431:308:12:Times:12:Times:C:ordonez@econ.upenn.edu
3:67:3380:0:34:72:197:707:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:1    Introduction
3:68:3397:34:22:72:540:673:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Governments finance their fiscal needs by selling bonds in sovereign debt auctions.  In
3:69:3484:22:22:72:540:651:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:these auctions, a large number of bonds are usually sold at one time to a large number
3:70:3570:22:21:72:540:629:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of  investors.   Investors  can  submit  multiple  bids  and  are  often  free  to  try  and  buy  as
3:71:3671:21:22:72:539:608:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:many units of the bonds as they can afford.1Given the set of submitted bids, auctions
3:72:3756:22:22:72:540:586:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:constitute a series of rules that determine the price(s) of newly issued sovereign bonds
3:73:3844:22:21:72:540:564:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and  the  corresponding  revenues  for  the  government  (or,  equivalently,  the  future  debt
3:74:3939:21:22:72:540:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:burden implied by the auction outcome). The results of sovereign debt auctions thus play
3:75:4027:22:22:72:540:521:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a critical role in determining governments’ cost of financing deficits, their implementation
3:76:4119:22:21:72:540:499:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of monetary policy, and even the extent to which they can successfully navigate internal
3:77:4207:21:22:72:266:478:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and external macroeconomic shocks.
3:78:4241:22:22:89:539:456:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Understanding the evolution of primary market sovereign bond prices has proven to
3:79:4322:22:21:72:540:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:be  challenging,  however.   Figure  1  illustrates  this  problem  using  interest  rate  data  for
3:80:4422:21:22:72:540:413:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:91-day CETES bonds issued by the Mexican government between 1978 and 2016.  These
3:81:4503:22:22:72:540:391:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bonds are domestically denominated, sold with small face values, and in large lots, to a
3:82:4591:22:21:72:540:369:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wide variety of investors, using auctions that alternated between discriminating (shaded
3:83:4679:21:22:72:539:348:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in the figure) and uniform price protocols.2During the long period displayed in the fig-
3:84:4767:22:22:71:539:326:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ure, annual bond yields went through periods of high turbulence (coincident to events
3:85:4852:22:21:71:539:304:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:such as the Latin American debt crisis of the 1980s and the ”Tequila Crisis” of 1995) and
3:86:4941:21:22:71:539:283:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:periods of prolonged stability (the 2000s).  Nevertheless, it has been difficult to attribute
3:87:5034:22:22:71:539:261:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:these price movements to shocks to particular set of “fundamentals,” such as GDP growth
3:88:5121:22:21:71:539:239:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:or  the  government’s  debt  service  policy.   Rather,  certain  shocks  seem  to  be  important
3:89:5218:21:22:71:539:218:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:drivers of bond yields during certain times but irrelevant in other periods.   Decipher-
3:90:5306:22:19:71:539:196:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ing the right mapping from shocks to prices is complicated by the fact that shocks will
3:91:5393:19:16:85:539:177:7:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:1Malvey, Archibald, and Flynn (1995) report that the U.S. Treasury typically receives 75-85 competitive
3:92:5496:16:12:72:540:161:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:bids or tenders, many of which come from the 37 primary deals. They also receive 850-900 noncompetitive
3:93:5599:12:8:72:464:149:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:tenders through the book-entry system and another 19,000 through TREASURY DIRECT.
3:94:5680:8:16:85:539:141:7:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:2Cetes are zero-coupon bonds which investors can obtain directly online by using Cetesdirecto since
3:95:5779:16:12:72:540:125:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:2010.  Cetes remain among the most important public debt instruments in Mexico.  In 2001, for example,
3:96:5881:12:12:72:540:113:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:Cetes alone represented 25% of all government securities, and were auctioned 180 times to 3,581 participat-
3:97:5988:12:11:72:540:101:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:ing bidders.  Mexico has switched the auction protocol in October 5, 2017 to uniform price auctions after
3:98:6093:11:0:72:348:90:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:more than two decades of using discriminatory-price auctions.
4:99:6155:0:22:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:typically differ in the mechanism by which they affect bond prices: while shocks to GDP
4:100:6242:22:22:72:540:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:growth or debt service are likely impact investors’ common value by altering the expected
4:101:6331:22:21:72:540:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:probability of default, liquidity or wealth shocks are more likely to affect private valua-
4:102:6422:21:22:72:540:643:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tions.  Furthermore, the information environment is likely to differ across shocks:  while
4:103:6512:22:22:72:540:621:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:some fundamentals, such as GDP growth or inflation are often publicly observable (albeit
4:104:6600:22:21:72:540:599:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:perhaps with a lag), others are difficult or costly too learn and evaluate.  In the Mexican
4:105:6691:21:22:72:540:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:context, a particularly pertinent example is knowledge of the inner workings of financial
4:106:6780:22:28:72:423:556:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f3:B:negotiations between Clinton and Congress over the 1995 bailout.3
4:107:6845:28:272:183:429:528:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:?:Figure 1: Mexican Bond Auction Interest Rates

4:129:6973:0:312:189:434:502:117:g_d0_f5:117:g_d0_f5:?:Banco	de	México91-day	Cetes	Interest	Rate	at	Auction
4:130:7025:312:21:89:539:190:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In line with these observations, Aguiar et al. (2016b) study emerging market interest
4:131:7110:21:22:72:540:169:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rate spreads (in secondary markets against LIBOR) and show that they vary substantially
4:132:7197:22:19:72:540:147:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:across  both  countries  and  time.   One  standard  explanation  for  this  variation  is  uncer-
4:133:7295:19:15:85:539:128:7:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:3On January 30, 1995, at exactly the moment when the Mexican government was informing the Clinton
4:134:7392:15:12:72:540:113:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:Administration that without an emergency injection of funds it would have to default, the Speaker of the
4:135:7496:12:12:72:540:101:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:House, Newt Gingrich, was informing the Clinton Administration that the bailout bill was stalled in the
4:136:7599:12:12:72:540:89:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:Congress.   See  Chun,  John  H.  ”Post-Modern  Sovereign  Debt  Crisis:  Did  Mexico  Need  an  International
4:137:7709:12:0:72:308:77:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:Bankruptcy Forum.” Fordham L. Rev. 64 (1995): 2647.
5:138:7761:0:22:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tainty about the likelihood of default or renegotiation.  While these spreads are partially
5:139:7852:22:22:72:540:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and occasionally accounted for by country fundamentals, like debt-to-output ratios or the
5:140:7941:22:21:72:540:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:growth rate of output, the high (on average) spreads on emerging market debt relative to
5:141:8029:21:22:72:540:643:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:actual defaults suggest that the pricing of these bonds include a substantial premium.
5:142:8115:22:22:72:540:621:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:While some the fluctuations in this premium can be accounted for with aggregate risk-
5:143:8200:22:21:72:540:599:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:pricing factors (like the aggregate price-earning ratio, which is a measure of the market
5:144:8289:21:22:72:540:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:price of risk,  or the VIX, which is a measure of the volatility premium),  the bulk of it
5:145:8379:22:22:72:168:556:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:seemingly cannot.
5:146:8396:22:21:89:539:534:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In this paper we argue that (potentially endogenous) changes in investor information
5:147:8480:21:22:72:540:513:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:may be an important driver of the observed premium on sovereign debt.  To make this
5:148:8563:22:22:72:540:491:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:point,  we  depart  from  the  standard  presumption  that  fundamentals  are  always  in  the
5:149:8657:22:21:72:540:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:information set of investors and explore how prices are determined if investors have to
5:150:8744:21:22:72:540:448:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:acquire at a cost information about non-public fundamentals (or pay a cost to process
5:151:8829:22:22:72:540:426:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:information about public fundamentals).   This introduces the possibility that investors
5:152:8917:22:21:72:540:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are asymmetric in their information sets,  and that this asymmetry is reflected in bond
5:153:9004:21:22:72:106:383:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:prices.
5:154:9011:22:22:89:539:361:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:To circumvent some of the challenges standard auction models face in determining
5:155:9091:22:21:72:540:339:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equilibrium prices, we propose a novel auction model with three key characteristics:  (i)
5:156:9180:21:22:72:540:318:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the good being auctioned is perfectly divisible, (ii) the number of bidders is large, and (iii)
5:157:9275:22:22:72:540:296:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:there is both common uncertainty about the good quality and about the mass of investors
5:158:9362:22:21:72:540:274:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:who participate in the auction. Given these three characteristics, the price-quantity strate-
5:159:9455:21:22:72:540:253:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:gic aspects of standard auction theory become less relevant, and a price-taking, or Wal-
5:160:9543:22:22:72:540:231:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rasian, analysis emerges as a good approximation.4With price-taking, instead of study-
5:161:9629:22:22:72:540:209:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f6:B:ing strategic bidding and information processing, we can focus on arational expectations
5:162:9717:22:21:72:540:187:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f3:B:equilibriumwhere the “market” is cleared using realistic auction rules.  We refer to such
5:163:9806:21:22:72:539:166:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:auction approximated by price-taking asWalrasian auctionsand show that they are par-
5:164:9890:22:19:72:540:144:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ticularly tractable, allowing for an analysis of the role of information in equilibrium price
5:165:9983:19:15:85:539:125:7:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:4Recent auction literature shows that price-taking arises as the number of bidders get large.  A recent
5:166:10086:15:12:72:540:110:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:example is Fudenberg, Mobius, and Szeidl (2007), who show that the equilibria of large double auctions
5:167:10188:12:12:72:540:98:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:with correlated private values are essentially fully revealing and approximate price-taking behavior when
5:168:10293:12:12:72:540:86:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:the number of bidders goes to infinity.  Another is Reny and Perry (2006) who show a similar result when
5:169:10397:12:0:72:330:74:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:bidders have affiliated values and prices are on a fine grid.
6:170:10459:0:22:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:determination and the role of auction rules in determining the volume and asymmetry
6:171:10542:22:22:72:540:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of information endogenously acquired by investors.  As a corollary, we show that using
6:172:10628:22:21:72:540:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:auction protocols may circumvent the Grossman and Stiglitz (1980) paradox:  there are
6:173:10713:21:22:72:540:643:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:strict incentives to acquire information even when equilibrium prices are fully revealing
6:174:10802:22:22:72:114:621:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ex-post.
6:175:10810:22:21:89:539:599:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:As with Cetes in Mexico, sovereign debt auctions worldwide are generally conducted
6:176:10892:21:22:72:540:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:using one of two formats: uniform-price or discriminatory. Discriminatory-price auctions
6:177:10980:22:22:72:540:556:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are slightly more prevalent, while the uniform-price auctions is the standard method used
6:178:11069:22:21:72:540:534:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in the United States.5Given the prevalence of both protocols, and the frequency at which
6:179:11157:21:22:72:540:513:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:some countries switch between protocols (as is clear for Mexico), we consider both types
6:180:11245:22:22:72:540:491:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of  auction  protocols  and  examine  their  implication  for  both  government  and  investor
6:181:11339:22:21:72:106:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:utility.
6:182:11347:21:22:89:539:448:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:To maintain tractability while allowing for asymmetric information, we will assume
6:183:11429:22:22:72:540:426:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that there are just two types of investors:  the informed who know more about bond’s
6:184:11513:22:21:72:540:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:default probability, and the uninformed who know less.  We are then able to character-
6:185:11599:21:22:72:540:383:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ize the rational expectations equilibria of our auction model under both auction formats
6:186:11687:22:22:72:540:361:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for different degrees of information asymmetry (as proxied by the fraction of informed
6:187:11773:22:21:72:540:339:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:investors). This success comes despite the fact that we deviate from the standard CARA-
6:188:11860:21:22:72:540:318:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:normal framework commonly used in portfolio choice models with asymmetric informa-
6:189:11942:22:22:72:540:296:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tion thereby allowing for investor wealth effects.6We view this as an attractive feature of
6:190:12033:22:21:71:539:274:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a theory of government bond yields, in that it may help the theory speak to bond yields
6:191:12120:21:22:71:266:253:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:during both normal times and crises.
6:192:12156:22:19:89:539:231:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:When the degree of asymmetric information among investors exogenous, we uncover
6:193:12235:19:16:85:539:212:7:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:5The heterogeneity of treasury auction formats is well-documented. For example, the U.S. switched to a
6:194:12337:16:12:72:540:196:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:uniform-price format from a discriminating-price format in the 1970s, while Canada and Germany use the
6:195:12439:12:12:72:540:184:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:price-discriminating format. Bartolini and Cottarelli (2001) study a sample in which 39 out of 42 countries
6:196:12546:12:11:72:540:172:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:use discriminatory price auctions. Brenner, Galai, and Sade (2009) analyze a sample of 48 countries, out of
6:197:12653:11:12:72:540:161:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:which 24 use discriminatory-price auctions, 9 use uniform-price auctions and the rest use either both or an
6:198:12760:12:9:72:180:149:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:hybrid between the two.
6:199:12783:9:15:85:539:140:7:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:6Portfolio choice models with asymmetric information in which prices do not perfectly reveal the quality
6:200:12887:15:12:72:540:125:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:of the bond ex-post are difficult to analyze because expectations, and hence excess demands, may not be
6:201:12990:12:12:72:540:113:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:continuous in the price of an asset.  It is well known that proving the existence of an equilibrium when
6:202:13094:12:12:72:540:101:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:prices are not fully revealing is very difficult (see Allen and Jordan (1998)), and that this challenge is usually
6:203:13208:12:0:72:526:89:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:tackled assuming CARA-normal cases because this combination yields a tractable linear price function.
7:204:13310:0:22:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a level-volatility trade-off between the two protocols. While uniform-price auctions gen-
7:205:13399:22:22:72:540:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:erate a higher sensitivity to demand shocks, the discriminatory-price auction generates
7:206:13486:22:21:72:540:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a higher debt burden (lower average prices for the bond).  Interestingly, this trade-off is
7:207:13577:21:22:72:540:643:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:only present when there is some degree of information asymmetry.  When information
7:208:13659:22:22:72:540:621:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(or the lack of information) is symmetric, both protocols are nearly identical in terms of
7:209:13749:22:21:72:364:599:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:average price and average exposure to demand shocks.
7:210:13801:21:22:89:539:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Our paper fills an important gap in the sovereign debt literature, which has typically
7:211:13887:22:22:72:540:556:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:focused on bond yields in secondary market,  but has neglected the specifics of how a
7:212:13972:22:21:72:540:534:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:government sells its bonds and the role of investors’ information in determining issue
7:213:14058:21:22:72:540:513:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:prices.  This is surprising since issue prices, rather than secondary market prices, enter
7:214:14148:22:22:72:540:491:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the government’s budget constraint.  To focus squarely on the determination of auction
7:215:14234:22:21:72:540:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:prices, we neglect some of the issues studied in the literature, but expand on others. First,
7:216:14327:21:22:72:540:448:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:most papers study  sovereign default as the outcome  of governments’ strategic choice,
7:217:14413:22:22:72:540:426:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:but use a parsimonious model of investor optimization. We take the opposite route, and
7:218:14499:22:21:72:540:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:focus on the auction mechanics and investors choices while entirely neglecting strategic
7:219:14587:21:22:72:540:383:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:considerations on the part of the government.7Second, most of the literature generates a
7:220:14675:22:22:71:539:361:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:fixed mapping between the bond quality and its price by assuming that investors are risk
7:221:14763:22:21:71:539:339:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:neutral and then requiring that the return, adjusted for the probability of default, equals
7:222:14854:21:22:71:539:318:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the risk-free rate.  We depart from these settings dramatically by assuming risk aversion
7:223:14943:22:22:71:539:296:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and specific auction clearing rules.  Finally,  while there has been some attention to the
7:224:15033:22:21:71:539:274:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:impact of the timing of decisions and of debt maturity in sovereign markets (see Aguiar
7:225:15120:21:22:71:539:253:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:et al. (2016a)), the actual mechanics of how sovereign bonds are sold in reality through
7:226:15208:22:22:71:539:231:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:auctions and their impact on observed prices has been ignored.  Our paper focuses on
7:227:15292:22:22:71:539:209:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:this neglected role of information acquisition in the context of an explicit auction model.
7:228:15383:22:21:71:539:187:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Addtionally, there has been a recent effort to empirically document the implications of
7:229:15470:21:22:71:539:166:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:different auction protocols and of the information sharing across dealers on the revenue
7:230:15558:22:22:71:539:144:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of governments.  For the former,  see the survey by Hortac ̧su (2011).  For the latter, see
7:231:15649:22:18:71:539:122:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Boyarchenko, Lucca, and Veldkamp (2017). Because our setting differs substantially from
7:232:15736:18:16:85:539:104:7:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:7See for  example Eaton  and Gersovitz  (1981),  the  review articles by  Aguiar and  Amador (2013)  and
7:233:15840:16:12:72:540:88:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:Aguiar et al. (2016b), and the recent quantitative literature by Aguiar and Gopinath (2006), Arellano (2008),
7:234:15949:12:0:72:328:76:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:Chatterjee and Eyigungor (2012), Bocola and Dovis (2016).
8:235:16007:0:22:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:these papers, we discuss in detail our paper’s relationship with this literature once we
8:236:16095:22:22:72:540:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:have presented our model.  Similarly, we also postpone a discussion of the broader rela-
8:237:16183:22:21:72:540:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tionship between our Walrasian auctions and the literature on general equilibrium theory
8:238:16271:21:53:72:143:643:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and auctions.
8:239:16284:53:40:72:476:590:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:2    Model with Exogenous Information Asymmetry
8:240:16331:40:30:72:190:550:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:2.1    Environment
8:241:16349:30:22:72:540:520:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:There are two periods, period 1 and period 2, and a single good (the numeraire).  The
8:242:16434:22:21:72:540:498:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:economy is populated by a measure one of ex-ante identical risk-averse investors, and
8:243:16519:21:22:72:539:477:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a government.   The government is modeled mechanically:  it needs to raiseDunits of
8:244:16602:22:22:71:539:455:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the numeraire in period one by auctioning (multiple units of) a bond that promises re-
8:245:16688:22:21:71:540:433:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:payment in period two.8Without loss of generality, we study zero-coupon pure-discount
8:246:16773:21:22:71:539:412:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bonds which promise a claim to one unit of the numeraire.  Bonds are risky because the
8:247:16859:22:22:71:539:390:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:government only delivers the promised payment if it does not default. If the government
8:248:16946:22:21:71:539:368:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:defaults, then investors cannot recover any of their investment.  If the amount of money
8:249:17034:21:22:71:539:347:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:raised at auction falls short ofD,  then government simply defaults on any bonds that
8:250:17119:22:22:71:539:325:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:it has already sold.  (We can also take this to mean that the government defaults on the
8:251:17207:22:21:71:250:303:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bonds coming due in period one).
8:252:17239:21:22:89:540:282:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The government’s default probability,κθis random and determined by the realization
8:253:17321:22:22:71:539:260:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of an exogenous state of the worldθ∈{g,b}. We assume thatκg< κband that the ex-ante
8:254:17404:22:21:71:539:238:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:probability of each state is given byf(g)andf(b)respectively, withf(g) +f(b) = 1. Since
8:255:17491:21:22:71:539:217:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the default probability determines the expected repayment of the bond, we refer to the
8:256:17577:22:22:71:539:195:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:realization ofκas aquality shock, where the bond withκgis agood quality bondand the one
8:257:17664:22:18:71:220:173:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f3:B:withκbis abad quality bond.9
8:258:17692:18:16:85:539:155:7:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:8The supply of bonds being auctioned to raiseDis therefore pinned down by the realized bids. This is
8:259:17792:16:8:72:444:139:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:meant to capture the impact of revenue needs on the government’s cost of financing.
8:260:17875:8:16:85:540:131:7:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f6:F:9It is straightforward to think of the possibleκθrealizations being themselves governed by anaggregate
8:261:17977:16:12:72:539:115:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f3:F:public shockνat the beginning of the period.   We anticipate that such a public shock would be likely to
8:262:18081:12:12:72:540:103:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:play an important role in accounting for data like that in Figure 1. However, since the analysis that follows
8:263:18190:12:0:72:306:91:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:remains the same, we do not explicitly incorporate it.
9:264:18245:0:22:89:539:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Investors consume only in the second period.  Accordingly, their objective is to maxi-
9:265:18331:22:22:72:540:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:mize their expected utility over second period consumption given a the strictly concave
9:266:18418:22:21:72:540:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:flow utility functionU.  Each investor has wealthWin period one and can either invest
9:267:18503:21:22:71:505:643:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in a risk-free bond (storage) or the risky bond being auctioned by the government.
9:268:18585:22:22:89:540:621:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:To allow for the possibility that prices are not fully revealing ofθex-post, we intro-
9:269:18671:22:21:71:540:599:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:duce ademand shock. Specifically, we assume that a random share of investorsηcannot
9:270:18754:21:22:71:539:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f7:B:participate in the auction and instead invests in the risk-free bond only. We assume thatη
9:271:18844:22:22:71:539:556:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is continuously distributed on the intervalH= [0,ηM]according to a continuous density
9:272:18929:22:21:71:540:534:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:functiong(η)that is nonzero everywhere on the interior of the interval, withηM<1. We
9:273:19013:21:22:71:532:513:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f7:B:will refer tos= (θ,η)as the state of the world and to the set of states byS={g,b}×H.
9:274:19097:22:22:89:539:491:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:A natural interpretations ofηis that it represents the fraction of investors who suffer
9:275:19184:22:21:71:539:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a liquidity or hedging shock.  Another is that some investors may randomly have access
9:276:19270:21:22:71:539:448:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to more favorable investment opportunities and thus do not invest in government bonds.
9:277:19356:22:22:71:540:426:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In the context of the auction literature,  the shock to demand coming throughηcan be
9:278:19440:22:21:71:540:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:therefore be thought of as acorrelated private value shock, while the shock to the quality
9:279:19530:21:22:71:539:383:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of the bond coming throughθis acommon value shock.  Note that the demand shock is
9:280:19611:22:22:71:539:361:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:isomorphic  to  a  supply  shock  due  to  which  the  government  needs  to  raiseDψat  the
9:281:19703:22:21:71:539:339:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:auction,  whereψ=  1/(1−η).   We  will  later  use  this  alternative  interpretation  in  our
9:282:19797:21:22:71:189:318:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:numerical illustration.
9:283:19820:22:22:89:539:296:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:There will be two types of investors at the auction: those who areinformed(I) about
9:284:19903:22:21:71:540:274:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:B:θand thus know its realization, and those who areuninformed(U) aboutθand do not
9:285:19982:21:22:71:539:253:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:know its realization.  We denote byi∈ {I,U}the type of investor and usen∈[0,1]to
9:286:20062:22:22:71:540:231:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:denote the share of informed investors.  The remaining share1−nthus consists of un-
9:287:20145:22:22:71:539:209:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:informed investors. The fractionnthus determines thedegree of asymmetric informationin
9:288:20231:22:21:71:539:187:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the sense that it measures the relative mass of investors with superior information about
9:289:20320:21:22:71:539:166:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the quality of the bond. Consistent with our mechanical modeling of the government we
9:290:20405:22:22:71:540:144:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:assume that it observes neitherθnorηbefore the auction.  This precludes signaling by
9:291:20489:22:21:71:539:122:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the government.  Because informed (uninformed) investors are otherwise identical, we
9:292:20573:21:22:71:539:101:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:can refer without loss of generality to a representative informed (uninformed) investor.
9:293:20661:22:0:71:540:79:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Neither type of investor is informed aboutη, which means that all investors face some
10:294:20747:0:22:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:uncertainty about the state of the world.  We will show below that this implies that all
10:295:20835:22:45:72:518:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:investors face uncertainty about the minimum price at which they can buy the bond.
10:296:20917:45:30:72:221:641:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:2.2    Auction Protocols
10:297:20941:30:22:72:540:611:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We  now  describe  the  auction  protocol  governing  which  investor  bids  the  government
10:298:21033:22:22:72:539:589:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:accepts and at which price accepted bids are executed.  Abidby an investor is defined
10:299:21118:22:21:72:540:567:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to be a pair{P,B}representing a commitment to purchaseBunits of the bond at a price
10:300:21201:21:22:72:540:546:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:no higher thanP, should the government decide to accept the bid.  Each investor is free
10:301:21288:22:22:72:540:524:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to submit as many bids as desired at the beginning of the auction. The government treats
10:302:21376:22:21:72:540:502:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:each bid independently, sorts all bids from the highest to the lowest bid price, and accepts
10:303:21468:21:22:72:540:481:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:all bids in descending order until it raisesDin revenue. We refer to the (highest possible)
10:304:21559:22:22:72:540:459:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:”lowest” accepted price as themarginal price ̄P.   All bids at prices above the marginal
10:305:21647:22:21:72:540:437:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:price are accepted;  all bids below are rejected.  Hence we refer to these bids above the
10:306:21736:21:22:72:540:416:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:marginal price asin the money, and to bids below the marginal price asout of the money.
10:307:21823:22:22:72:540:394:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(If there is excess demand at the marginal price, we assume that the government rations
10:308:21910:22:21:72:387:372:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bids pro-rata. This does not occur in equilibrium, however.)
10:309:21970:21:22:89:539:351:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Investors lack commitment in two important dimensions. First, they cannot commit to
10:310:22053:22:22:72:540:329:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:honor any intertemporal contracts. We will take this to mean that they cannot borrow at
10:311:22140:22:21:72:540:307:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the riskfree rate, nor can they short-sell the bond at the auction. Investors must therefore
10:312:22232:21:22:72:539:286:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bid nonnegative quantities (B≥0) and can spend no more than their wealthWon bonds.
10:313:22314:22:22:72:540:264:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Second, they cannot commit to credibly share their information aboutθ. Hence investors
10:314:22400:22:21:72:540:242:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cannot directly acquire information from other investors.  A unit of the bond is a claim
10:315:22488:21:22:72:540:221:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to a real unit of the numeraire in period two.  As this claim either pays 1 or 0, the range
10:316:22579:22:22:72:540:199:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of possible prices isP∈[0,1].   Since investors will typically find it optimal to submit
10:317:22667:22:21:72:539:177:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:multiple bids, we start by taking the investors’ strategy to be a bid functionBI(P|θ)for
10:318:22755:21:22:72:308:156:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the informed andBU(P)for the uninformed.
10:319:22795:22:22:89:539:134:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The price at which an accepted bid is executed depends on the auction protocol.  We
10:320:22878:22:21:72:540:112:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:consider two protocols that are widely used in a large multi-unit auctions of common-
10:321:22963:21:0:72:539:91:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:value goods, not just sovereign bonds. The first is thediscriminatory-price(DP) auction in
11:322:23054:0:22:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:which all accepted bids are executed at the bid price (“pay as you bid”). The second is the
11:323:23145:22:22:72:539:686:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f3:B:uniform-price(UP) auction in which all accepted bids are executed at the lowest accepted
11:324:23233:22:21:71:502:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(or marginal) price. Government and investors take the auction protocol as given.
11:325:23314:21:22:89:540:643:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Denote the marginal price in statesby ̄P(s).  In a UP auction,  the amount that the
11:326:23397:22:40:71:230:621:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:government raises in statesis
11:327:23426:40:0:165:201:581:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:C:(1−η)
11:328:23431:0:26:202:225:598:12:g_d0_f14:8:g_d0_f15:?:[∫1
11:329:23434:26:0:217:232:572:8:g_d0_f15:8:g_d0_f15:?: ̄P(s)
11:330:23440:0:10:235:240:591:12:g_d0_f14:12:g_d0_f14:C:[
11:331:23441:10:0:240:389:581:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f10:C:nBI(P|θ(s)) + (1−n)BU(P)
11:332:23465:0:10:389:394:591:12:g_d0_f14:12:g_d0_f14:C:]
11:333:23466:10:0:396:410:581:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:C:dP
11:334:23468:0:14:411:417:598:12:g_d0_f14:12:g_d0_f14:A:]
11:335:23469:14:43:422:446:584:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f7:C: ̄P(s),
11:336:23476:43:22:72:539:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:whereθ(s)is the quality shock that corresponds to states.The government’s revenue is
11:337:23560:22:22:72:539:519:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:thus simply the marginal price ̄P(s)multiplied by the accepted number of in the money
11:338:23645:22:21:72:539:497:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bids at the marginal price. Revenue is increasing in the marginal price ̄P(s), but the num-
11:339:23736:21:22:72:540:476:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ber of accepted bids is decreasing in the marginal price. A government that needs to raise
11:340:23826:22:22:72:540:454:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:more funds will thus have to accept a lower marginal price.  As the auction clears when
11:341:23913:22:21:72:540:432:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the demand equalsDthere may be multiple marginal prices at which the government
11:342:23992:21:22:72:539:411:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:raisesD.  As we are not interested in this particular source of multiplicity, we will focus
11:343:24083:22:22:72:342:389:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on the equilibrium with the highest marginal price.
11:344:24134:22:39:89:443:367:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In a DP auction, the amount that the government raises in statesis
11:345:24200:39:0:172:208:328:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:C:(1−η)
11:346:24205:0:25:210:232:344:12:g_d0_f14:8:g_d0_f15:?:[∫1
11:347:24208:25:0:224:239:319:8:g_d0_f15:8:g_d0_f15:A: ̄P(s)
11:348:24214:0:9:242:247:337:12:g_d0_f14:12:g_d0_f14:C:[
11:349:24215:9:0:247:397:328:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f10:C:nBI(P|θ(s)) + (1−n)BU(P)
11:350:24239:0:9:396:401:337:12:g_d0_f14:12:g_d0_f14:C:]
11:351:24240:9:0:403:426:328:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:C:PdP
11:352:24243:0:16:428:434:344:12:g_d0_f14:12:g_d0_f14:A:]
11:353:24244:16:42:436:439:328:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:A:.
11:354:24245:42:22:72:539:286:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In contrast to the UP auction, revenue is always declining in the marginal price ̄P(s). This
11:355:24337:22:21:72:540:264:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is because executed prices are fixed at the bidding price while the number of accepted
11:356:24423:21:22:72:540:243:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bids is decreasing in the marginal price. The marginal price is defined such that the gov-
11:357:24513:22:22:72:540:221:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ernment’s revenue is equal toD.  Hence it is immediately clear that a government that
11:358:24598:22:45:72:399:199:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:needs to raise more funds must accept a lower marginal price.
11:359:24659:45:30:72:158:154:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:2.3    Bidding
11:360:24673:30:21:72:540:124:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Investors have rational expectations: the set of marginal prices, their probabilities, and the
11:361:24767:21:22:72:540:103:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:states associated with each marginal price are all common knowledge when submitting
11:362:24850:22:0:72:540:81:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bids.  After the auction is completed and the realization of the marginal price has been
12:363:24940:0:22:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:revealed,  informed and uninformed investors can make inferences with respect to the
12:364:25024:22:22:72:539:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f7:B:state.  This is straightforward for informed investors since they knowθand can inferη
12:365:25109:22:21:72:540:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f10:B:by inverting the price schedule. Inference is harder for the uninformed. If the price ̄P(s)
12:366:25200:21:22:72:540:643:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is uniquely generated by a quality shock, then they too can infer the state perfectly.  If
12:367:25290:22:22:72:540:621:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:there are two states(g,ηg)and(b,ηb)with a common price, then they will still be able to
12:368:25377:22:21:72:540:599:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:update their beliefs about the set of possible states and their probabilities from observing
12:369:25469:21:22:72:540:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the price. However, they will not be able to uniquely identify the true state. Importantly,
12:370:25560:22:22:72:540:556:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:this ex-post information is of limited use because all of the investors must choose their
12:371:25649:22:21:72:540:534:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bidspriorto observing the realized marginal price.  Inference thus helps investors form
12:372:25736:21:22:72:540:513:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:expectations  regarding  the  states  in  which  a  given  bid  at  pricePis  accepted,  but  the
12:373:25833:22:22:72:540:491:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:auction format precludes them from revising their bids given the information contained
12:374:25919:22:21:72:540:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in prices ex-post. This ex-ante commitment to bids distinguishes our auction model from
12:375:26006:21:22:72:540:448:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:canonical noisy rational expectations models such as Grossman and Stiglitz (1980).  The
12:376:26093:22:22:72:539:426:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:advantage of informed investors is that they knowθwhen submitting bids, and thus face
12:377:26178:22:21:72:540:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:uncertaintly only about the values ofηfor which a given bid is accepted.  Uninformed
12:378:26262:21:22:72:539:383:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:investors instead face uncertainty about bothθandηwhen forecasting the set of states
12:379:26346:22:22:72:270:361:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for which a given bid is in the money.
12:380:26384:22:18:89:539:339:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In a DP auction, it is a strictly dominant strategy to bid only at possible marginal prices
12:381:26475:18:25:74:539:321:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f3:B: ̄P(s). If the investor were to bid at a slightly higher price, the bid is accepted in the same
12:382:26570:25:22:72:540:296:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:states but the investors pays a higher price.  In the UP auction it is a weakly dominating
12:383:26660:22:21:72:540:274:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:strategy to do so. We thus restrict investors to only bid at marginal prices. This means that
12:384:26753:21:22:72:540:253:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:we no longer need to think of our investors having a bidding strategy for each possible
12:385:26840:22:22:72:540:231:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:price but instead think of them as choosing how many bonds to bid for at the marginal
12:386:26925:22:22:72:538:209:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f7:B:price for each state.  Since bids only happen at marginal prices, we drop the notation ̄P
12:387:27014:22:31:71:488:187:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and just refer toP. We also switch to a starker specification for bids and prices.
12:388:27096:31:22:71:539:156:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f6:F:Definition 1.For each states= (θ,η)∈ S,the marginal price isP(θ,η).  The set of marginal
12:389:27184:22:21:71:540:134:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:prices isP.An action for an uninformed investor is a functionBU(θ,η)denoting the number
12:390:27271:21:22:71:540:113:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f10:F:of  bids  at  marginal  priceP(θ,η).An  action  for  an  informed  investor  is  a  functionBI(θ,η|ˆθ)
12:391:27373:22:0:71:506:91:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f7:C:denoting the number of bids at marginal priceP(θ,η)when the realized quality shock isˆθ.
13:392:27463:0:22:72:539:708:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f6:F:Remark 1.Bids in any two states(g,ηg)and(b,ηb)such thatP(g,ηg) =P(b,ηb),are perfect
13:393:27546:22:22:71:539:686:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:substitutes since they are accepted and rejected in the identical sets of states.  Thus, the investor
13:394:27647:22:31:71:524:664:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f7:C:just chooses the total quantityB(g,ηg) +B(b,ηb)to bid at the priceP=P(g,ηg) =P(b,ηb).
13:395:27732:31:22:71:540:633:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f6:F:Remark 2.This stark specification allows us to directly compare our auction to a competitive
13:396:27824:22:22:71:539:611:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:equilibrium.  It is also particularly helpful when the set ofη’s is finite, so that the set of possible
13:397:27927:22:21:71:539:589:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:marginal prices is as well. In our original specification of actions as bids on the set of all potential
13:398:28031:21:22:71:540:568:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:pricesP∈[0,1]this would mean that the bid function would be positive only at a finite set of
13:399:28123:22:22:71:540:546:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:points corresponding to those marginal prices. But even whenηis continuous, the set of marginal
13:400:28218:22:52:71:317:524:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:C:prices is a strict subset of the set of potential prices.
13:401:28275:52:40:71:262:472:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:3    Auction Equilibrium
13:402:28299:40:30:71:171:432:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:3.1    Definition
13:403:28316:30:22:71:539:402:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We start defining the problem of the uninformed investor. If the government ends up de-
13:404:28403:22:21:71:539:380:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:faulting in the second period, the uninformed investor simply consumes the unit payoff
13:405:28489:21:22:71:539:359:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:from his risk-free bonds, which we denote byBURF(s).If the government does not default,

16:581:33800:21:22:72:540:252:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:auction.   This is because accepted bids are executed at the bid price,  not the marginal
16:582:33889:22:22:72:540:230:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:price. Hence total revenue in stateswhen evaluated atP( ̃s)is always smaller than when
16:583:33975:22:21:72:540:208:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:evaluated atP(s)< P( ̃s)because fewer bids are executed.  The bid-overhang constraint
16:584:34060:21:22:72:540:187:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:can and does bind in the UP auction,  however.   The reason is that there is a trade-off

16:587:34316:21:29:72:151:122:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:atP(s)< P( ̃s).

17:590:34480:0:32:86:358:708:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:A:1.  each investor type’s bid function solves their problem,
17:591:34539:32:32:86:387:676:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f7:A:2.  the auction-clearing condition(11)is satisfied for alls∈S,
17:592:34601:32:34:86:357:644:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f7:A:3.  the bid-overhang constraint is satisfied at eachs∈S.
17:593:34657:34:22:72:540:610:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f6:F:Remark 3.Formulating an equilibrium in this stark fashion, where bids are defined as functions
17:594:34751:22:22:72:540:588:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:directly of the state, is isomorphic to a more standard formulation where bids are defined as func-
17:595:34850:22:21:72:539:566:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:tions of prices.  The price functions are the same, asBU(P(s)) =BU(s)and0elsewhere, while
17:596:34939:21:22:72:539:545:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f6:F:BI(P(s),θ)  =BI(s,θ)and0elsewhere.  The main difference is that the standard formulation
17:597:35027:22:22:72:540:523:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:defines the bid function overallpotential prices rather than marginal prices only.  Even though
17:598:35122:22:21:72:540:501:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:the two formulations are formally identical, the standard formulation is poorly behaved computa-
17:599:35218:21:22:72:540:480:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:tionally as the bid function is discontinuous around marginal prices given that no investor bids at
17:600:35317:22:31:72:172:458:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:C:non-marginal prices.
17:601:35337:31:22:72:540:427:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f6:F:Proposition  1.For  both  UP  and  DP  auctions,  the  price  functionP(θ,η)is  decreasing  inη.
17:602:35433:22:32:71:492:405:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:C:Conditional onθ, the price function is continuous and differentiable almost everywhere.
17:603:35520:32:21:71:540:373:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f3:B:Proof.For the DP auction, monotonicity inηfollows directly from the auction-clearing
17:604:35604:21:22:71:539:352:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:condition, while for the UP auction it follows from the bid-overhang constraint.  Mono-
17:605:35691:22:22:71:539:330:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tonicity and boundedness of the price function then imply continuity and differentiability
17:606:35781:22:31:71:303:308:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:almost everywhere by Lebesgue’s Theorem.
17:607:35821:31:22:72:540:277:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f6:F:Corollary 2.A bid made at priceP(θ,η)is in-the-money for allˆη≥ηgivenθ, and if there exists
17:608:35912:22:45:71:490:255:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f7:C:a ̄ηsuch thatP( ̄θ, ̄η) =P(θ,η)for ̄θ6=θ, then it is in-the-money for allˆη≥ ̄ηgiven ̄θ.
17:609:36000:45:30:71:539:210:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:F:3.2    Comparison of Auction Equilibrium and Competitive Equilibrium
17:610:36068:30:22:71:539:180:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Now we have defined an auction equilibrium, we can compare its structure with that of a
17:611:36155:22:21:71:539:158:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:competitive equilibrium, defined as a tuple consisting of a equilibrium price and demand
17:612:36243:21:22:71:485:137:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:functions such that there is no excess supply of bonds at the equilibrium price.
17:613:36323:22:22:89:539:115:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:It is evident that a DP auction equilibrium cannot be a competitive equilibrium: there
17:614:36409:22:22:71:539:93:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is a single market-clearing price in the latter, while bonds trade at multiple distinct prices
17:615:36503:22:0:71:539:71:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in the former. In UP auctions, however, bonds are always sold at a single price. In many
18:616:36593:0:22:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cases,  a UP auction equilibrium will therefore turn out to be isomorphic to a standard
18:617:36680:22:22:72:521:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:competitive equilibrium with heterogeneous information. We establish this link here.
18:618:36764:22:21:89:539:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In UP auctions, uninformed investors chooseBU(s)to maximize(1)subject to con-
18:619:36841:21:22:72:539:643:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:straints(2),(3)and the short-sale constraint(5)(see Definition 2).  The decision problem
18:620:36929:22:22:72:540:621:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in a competitive equilibrium is identical except for the fact that the short-sale constraint
18:621:37021:22:21:72:539:599:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:applies tototalpurchases of bonds in each states,  rather than bid-by-bid.   That is,  in
18:622:37110:21:40:72:485:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:competitive equilibrium we replace (5) with a short-sale constraint of the form
18:623:37189:40:40:217:540:538:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f3:A:BUR(s)≥0andBURF(s)≥0∀s∈S.(13)
18:624:37218:40:21:89:539:498:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The same considerations hold for the informed investor.  To check whether a UP auc-
18:625:37301:21:22:71:539:477:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tion equilibrium is isomorphic to a competitive equilibrium, it is thus sufficient to verify
18:626:37393:22:22:71:539:455:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:whether or not constraints(5)and(13)(and their analogues for the informed investor)
18:627:37476:22:21:71:539:433:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:imply each other.  To go from constraint(5)to(13)we can construct the associated total
18:628:37562:21:22:72:540:412:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:risky bond purchases just by summing  over the in-the-money bids.  This implies that if
18:629:37649:22:22:72:358:390:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f3:B:(5)does not bind in any states, then neither does(13).
18:630:37703:22:21:89:540:368:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:To go from constraint(13)to(5), we can construct the associated state-by-state bids
18:631:37786:21:22:72:539:347:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:given the total bond purchases in a competitive equilibrium,{BIR(s,θ),BUR(s)}, using the
18:632:37874:22:40:72:540:325:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:difference between the risky bond purchases atsand those at the next highest prices′, i.e.
18:633:37964:40:39:242:540:285:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:A:BU(s) =BUR(s)−BUR(s′),(14)
18:634:37990:39:22:72:539:246:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:whereP(s′) = min{P(s′′)> P(s)}for alls′′∈S. The analogous object for the informed is
18:635:38074:22:22:72:408:224:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f3:B:constructed using their conditional total purchasesBIR(s,θ(s)).11
18:636:38139:22:21:89:539:202:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We can then distinguish three scenarios.  First, if the state-by-state bids are nonnega-
18:637:38227:21:22:72:540:181:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tive in the UP auction equilibrium so that (5) does not bind, then the short-sale constraint
18:638:38319:22:22:72:540:159:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cannot bind for total purchases and there is an associated competitive equilibrium.  Sec-
18:639:38408:22:21:72:540:137:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ond, if there is a state in which the short-sale constraint (5) binds in the UP auction equi-
18:640:38501:21:19:72:540:116:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:librium, there is an associated competitive equilibrium only if the short-sale constraint
18:641:38590:19:19:82:539:97:7:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:11As highlighted in Footnote 10, the mathematically accurate expression for states={ ̄θ, ̄η}when de-
18:642:38690:19:0:72:357:78:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f18:F:mand shocks are continuously distributed isBU(s)≡BU( ̄θ, ̄η) =
18:643:38752:0:10:360:371:85:10:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f14:?:∑
18:644:38753:10:0:370:374:75:7:g_d0_f12:7:g_d0_f12:A:θ
18:645:38754:0:9:378:410:83:7:g_d0_f12:7:g_d0_f19:?:dBUR(θ,η)
18:646:38763:9:0:390:413:74:7:g_d0_f12:10:g_d0_f3:?:dη.
19:647:38768:0:22:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on total risky bond purchases also binds and total bids are zero.  Third, there is no as-
19:648:38857:22:22:72:540:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sociated competitive equilibrium when there are states for which the nonnegativity con-
19:649:38944:22:21:72:540:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:straint does not bind for total purchases in the competitive equilibrium, but do bind for
19:650:39033:21:22:72:540:643:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:individual bids in particular states in the UP auction. Hence UP auction equilibria are not
19:651:39124:22:22:72:540:621:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:necessarily isomorphic to competitive equilibria. The next proposition formalizes this dis-
19:652:39215:22:21:72:540:599:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cussion.  Later on, we use this insight to guide our discussion of information acquisition
19:653:39305:21:22:72:540:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:incentives in auctions relative to canonical competitive models in the spirit of Grossman
19:654:39394:22:32:72:167:556:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and Stiglitz (1980)
19:655:39413:32:21:72:539:524:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f6:F:Proposition 3.A UP auction equilibrium{P(s),BI(s,θ),BU(s)}in which the short-sale con-
19:656:39499:21:22:72:540:503:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:straint on risky bond purchases only binds when total risky bond purchases are 0 for alls∈Shas
19:657:39593:22:22:72:539:481:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:an associated competitive equilibrium{P(s),BUCE(s),BICE(s,θ)}.  Any competitive equilibrium
19:658:39684:22:21:72:539:459:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f6:F:{P(s),BICE(s,θ),BUCE(S)}in which the associated bids{BI(s,θ),BU(s)}constructed using (14)
19:659:39773:21:32:72:490:438:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:C:are nonnegative and satisfy the bid-overhang constraint (12) is an auction equilibrium.
19:660:39860:32:22:89:539:406:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Even  if  the  differences  in  short-sale  constraints  in  competitive  equilibrium  and  the
19:661:39955:22:21:72:540:384:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:auction auction do not matter, so that the auction equilibrium has an associated compet-
19:662:40043:21:22:72:540:363:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:itive equilibrium,  there is another condition that is unique to the auction protocol and
19:663:40132:22:22:72:540:341:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:may break the mapping between the two equilibria: the bid-overhang constraint. Hence
19:664:40216:22:21:72:540:319:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the set of UP auction equilibria is a subset of the set of competitive equilibria.   In the
19:665:40307:21:46:72:504:298:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:numerical examples, we will illustrate the mechanics underlying this observation.
19:666:40388:46:30:72:284:252:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:3.3    Investor’s Optimal Bidding

20:727:41924:40:30:72:229:200:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:3.3.2    Uninformed Investors
20:728:41953:30:22:72:540:170:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Now consider the uninformed investors’ problem.   Since these investors do not know
20:729:42036:22:22:72:539:148:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the  realizedθ,  they  must  form  expectations  regarding  the  quality  of  bond  conditional
20:730:42131:22:21:72:540:126:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on a given bid being executed.  In order to rewrite the problem in terms of the expected
20:731:42219:21:22:72:540:105:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:probability of default conditional on the realized marginal price, we first explain how this

22:847:44741:40:21:72:540:254:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Comparing this expression to the informed investors’ first-order condition, it is clear that
22:848:44833:21:22:72:540:233:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the uninformed face the same basic tradeoffs as the informed, but weighted by the ex-
22:849:44918:22:22:72:540:211:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:pected default probability rather than the true default probability.  As we show below,
22:850:45005:22:21:72:540:189:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:this leads to a form of adverse selection:  when bidding at high marginal prices,  unin-
22:851:45093:21:22:72:540:168:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:formed investors also expect these bids to be accepted after bad quality shocks, leading to
22:852:45184:22:22:72:540:146:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a downward revision of expected asset quality.  Uninformed investors thus have weaker
22:853:45269:22:31:72:417:124:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:marginal incentives to bid at high prices than informed investors.
22:854:45335:31:22:72:540:93:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f6:F:Proposition 4.Fixing the price scheduleP(s), both the informed and the uninformed bidders do
22:855:45427:22:0:72:540:71:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:strictly better under the UP protocol than the DP protocol so long as there exists a set ofη’s of
23:856:45526:0:32:72:407:708:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:C:positive measure at which they they are making positive bids, fixingθ.
23:857:45596:32:22:72:539:676:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f3:B:Proof.The uninformed (informed) UP bidders simply have to replicate the bids of the
23:858:45679:22:21:72:539:654:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:uninformed (informed) DP bidders.  Note that sinceP(θ,η1)> P(θ,η2)ifη1< η2, they
23:859:45759:21:22:72:539:633:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:have lower expenditures on the risky bond in state(θ,η2)under the UP protocol that they
23:860:45846:22:22:72:540:611:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:would under the DP protocol if they have positive bids in these two states.  Hence they
23:861:45933:22:21:72:540:589:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:have higher purchases of the risk-free bond in(θ,η2).  This raises their consumption in
23:862:46020:21:31:72:316:568:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:both the default and the repayment outcomes.
23:863:46064:31:22:89:539:537:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Since, fixing prices, the investors are always better off under the UP than the DP auc-
23:864:46151:22:21:72:540:515:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tions, it follows that the government can only prefer the UP auction if it delivers higher
23:865:46241:21:22:72:540:494:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:prices in some appropriate average sense.  Whether this will be the case is unclear since
23:866:46330:22:22:72:540:472:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the substitution effect will encourage higher bidding under UP, but the income effect com-
23:867:46420:22:21:72:540:450:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ing through the lower expenditures can have an ambiguous affect depending upon the
23:868:46502:21:53:72:246:429:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:curvature of the utility fuctionU.
23:869:46536:53:34:72:446:376:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:4    Characterization of UP Auction Equilibrium
23:870:46583:34:22:72:540:342:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We  now  characterize  uniform-price  auction  equilibrium.   (The  characterization  of  the
23:871:46676:22:22:72:540:320:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:discriminatory-price  auction  equilibrium  is  in  Section  5).   In  particular,  we  show  how
23:872:46773:22:21:72:539:298:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equilibrium prices depend on the fraction of informed investorsn.  We later use this to
23:873:46860:21:22:72:540:277:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:compute sovereign bond yields, the government’s debt burden and investors’ incentives
23:874:46945:22:22:72:540:255:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to acquire information givenn.  Accordingly, we will usePUP(s;n)to denote the price
23:875:47028:22:21:71:539:233:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:function for each state and degree of asymmetric information in the UP auction.  When
23:876:47113:21:22:71:540:212:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:there is no risk of confusion, we will simply writeP(s).  In a similar fashion, we will use
23:877:47204:22:22:71:540:190:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:B:BUP,U(s;n)for the bids of the uninformed andBUP,I(s,θ;n)for the bids of the informed,
23:878:47289:22:45:71:506:168:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:but use the simpler notationBU(s)andBI(s,θ)when there is no risk of confusion.
23:879:47367:45:30:71:259:123:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:4.1    Symmetric Benchmarks
23:880:47394:30:21:71:540:93:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f6:B:We begin by considering the two symmetric benchmarks: thesymmetric ignorance equilib-
23:881:47479:21:0:71:539:72:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f3:B:riumin which no investor is informed (n= 0), and thesymmetric information equilibriumin
24:882:47568:0:40:72:285:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:which all investors are informed (n= 1).

24:947:49007:40:21:71:539:99:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f6:F:Remark 4(Value of Information atn= 0).What is the value of information when noone else
24:948:49093:21:0:71:539:78:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:is informed?  A single atomistic informed investor who is informed when noone else is faces the

25:951:49387:22:21:72:539:664:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:size of(16)is increasingκand the right-hand side is decreasing, an atomistic informed investor
25:952:49481:21:22:72:540:643:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:earns a higher expected payoff by bidding more than the uninformed in the good state and less in
25:953:49577:22:40:72:135:621:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:C:the bad state.
25:954:49591:40:30:72:236:581:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:4.1.2    Symmetric Information

25:979:50160:40:21:71:540:363:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f6:F:Remark 5(Value of Information atn= 1).What is the cost of being uninformed when everyone
25:980:50248:21:22:71:539:342:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:else is informed? The answer may be zero. Specifically, UP auctions can generate a result similar
25:981:50345:22:22:71:539:320:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:to canonical rational expectations models with asymmetric information, namely that uninformed
25:982:50438:22:21:71:539:298:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:investors may be able to replicate the portfolio and payoffs of informed investors. The next section
25:983:50538:21:40:71:309:277:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:C:characterizes conditions such that this is the case.
25:984:50590:40:30:71:170:237:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:4.1.3    Replication
25:985:50610:30:22:71:539:207:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In competitive equilibrium, there are no gains from acquiring information if prices are
25:986:50697:22:22:71:539:185:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:fully revealing (Grossman and Stiglitz 1980).  A similar result holds in UP auction equi-
25:987:50786:22:21:71:539:163:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:librium, but under more stringent conditions. These additional restrictions arise because
25:988:50875:21:32:71:501:142:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bids cannot be adjusted ex-post conditional on the information revealed in prices.
25:989:50957:32:22:71:540:110:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f6:F:Proposition 5.In a UP auction, uninformed investors can replicate the total bids and ex-post
25:990:51049:22:0:71:515:88:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:C:payoffs of informed investors in every state (and hence informed investors’ ex-ante payoff) if:
26:991:51146:0:32:86:505:708:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f7:A:1.  Prices are fully revealing: each marginal price is associated with a unique state inS.
26:992:51236:32:21:86:540:676:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:A:2.  Ordering marginal prices and associated total bids of the informed from the highest to the
26:993:51330:21:30:101:540:655:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:A:lowest marginal price, the total bids of the informed are weakly ranked from lowest to highest.
26:994:51425:30:22:72:539:625:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f3:B:Proof.Condition 1 ensures that the uninformed can accurately infer the state in which
26:995:51510:22:21:72:540:603:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:each bid is accepted.  Condition 2 second ensures that the no short-sale constraint does
26:996:51598:21:30:72:278:582:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:not bind for marginal bids in any state.
26:997:51638:30:22:72:540:552:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f6:F:Definition 6.Replication isfeasibleif the conditions in Proposition 5 are satisfied. Replication
26:998:51734:22:30:71:236:530:12:g_d0_f27:12:g_d0_f6:C:failsif the conditions are violated.
26:999:51770:30:22:71:540:500:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f7:F:Corollary 6.The conditions in Proposition 5 are satisfied in a UP auction equilibrium withn
26:1000:51861:22:30:71:489:478:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:C:informed investors ifP(g,ηM;n)> P(b,0;n)andBIR([g,ηM],g;n)<BIR([b,0],b;n).
26:1001:51935:30:21:72:540:448:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f3:B:Proof.P(θ,η)is strictly decreasing inηby Proposition 1, and so informed investors’ bids
26:1002:52022:21:22:72:539:427:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f7:B:quantities are strictly increasing inηgivenθ.  The first condition implies thatP(g,η)>
26:1003:52108:22:22:72:539:405:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:B:P(b,η′)for allη,η′, and soP(s)6=P(s′)for anys,s′∈ S.  Hence all uninformed bids on
26:1004:52190:22:21:71:539:383:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the high-price schedule are accepted in the bad state.  The second condition ensures that
26:1005:52279:21:22:71:539:362:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the short-sale constraint does not bind for uninformed investors in the bad state when
26:1006:52365:22:30:71:252:340:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:replicating the informed portfolio.
26:1007:52400:30:22:89:539:310:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Even if uninformed investors can replicate the informed portfolio, they will generally
26:1008:52486:22:21:72:540:288:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:not make the samemarginal bidsas the informed in every state. The reason is that, unlike
26:1009:52574:21:22:72:540:267:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the bids of the informed, all of the bids by uninformed investors on theθ=gschedule
26:1010:52657:22:22:71:539:245:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are also accepted whenθ=b.To replicate the informed portfolio, the uninformed must
26:1011:52739:22:21:71:539:223:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f6:B:therefore make the same marginal bids as the informed at prices on thehigh-quality sched-
26:1012:52828:21:22:71:539:202:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f3:B:ule, but bid less than the informed on the low-quality schedule.  The cumulation of bids
26:1013:52916:22:22:71:539:180:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on both schedules is then such that the total bond holdings are identical to those of the
26:1014:53005:22:21:71:539:158:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:informed. This observation also provides intuition as to when replication fails: if the sec-
26:1015:53097:21:22:71:539:137:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ond condition is violated, then the number of bonds accumulated through bids on the
26:1016:53180:22:22:71:539:115:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:high-quality price schedule is so high that the uninformed would have to bid negative
26:1017:53265:22:22:71:539:93:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:amounts on the low-quality schedule in order to obtain the same total portfolio. But this
26:1018:53354:22:0:71:280:71:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is ruled out by the short-sale constraint.
27:1019:53398:0:31:72:499:708:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:4.2    Asymmetric Information: Special Case with Log Preferences

27:1030:53906:0:39:392:395:551:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:C:,
27:1031:53907:39:22:72:539:512:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:where ̃κi(s)is investori’s inferred default probability given that the bid was accepted at
27:1032:53997:22:0:71:217:490:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f10:C:P(s), andBiRFandBiR(s) =
27:1033:54021:0:14:221:227:500:12:g_d0_f14:12:g_d0_f14:A:∫

30:1164:60303:22:21:71:539:562:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The combination of short-sale constraints and uninformed investors’ endogenous belief
30:1165:60388:21:22:71:539:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:leads to the possibility of endogenous jumps in demand and, as a consequence, multiple
30:1166:60474:22:22:71:539:519:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equilibria.  Unfortunately, the endogeneity of beliefs means that the model is no longer

31:1218:62610:22:21:72:539:272:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:verge to each other asn→0.  In the intervaln∈(0,ηM]instead, the bid-overhang con-
31:1219:62691:21:22:72:540:251:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:straint binds and price schedules overlap. To illustrate the resulting equilibrium, we plot

31:1221:62866:22:21:72:540:207:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:overhang constraint binds in all three cases. Since per-capita bids are increasing inψcon-
31:1222:62956:21:22:72:540:186:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ditional onθ, moreover, the state-contingent price schedules first overlap in the pair of
31:1223:63045:22:22:72:540:164:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:states(b,1)and(g,ˆψg(n)), whereˆψg(n)is defined such that uninformed investors’ good-
31:1224:63130:22:21:72:539:142:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:state bids evaluated atP(g,ψg)are sufficient to cover the supply of bonds in(b,1).  (See
31:1225:63218:21:22:72:540:121:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the proof of Proposition 9 for an analogous construction.) Hence, the region of overlap is
31:1226:63308:22:22:72:478:99:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:such that fewer investors participate conditional on a good than a bad shock.
31:1227:63385:22:0:89:539:77:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Multiple  equilibria  with  different  prices  can  be  sustained  in  our  model  due  to  the
32:1228:63482:0:22:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:following logic. Suppose first that the common price is low and the short-sale constraint
32:1229:63571:22:22:72:540:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:does not bind,P <1−κb. (This threshold is plotted using pink-dotted horizontal lines.)
32:1230:63657:22:21:71:539:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Uninformed investors then infer from the low price that the bond is likely to be of low
32:1231:63744:21:22:71:539:643:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:quality,  and reduce their demand.   But informed investors continue to buy,  and fewer
32:1232:63831:22:22:71:539:621:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:investors suffer a demand shock ifθ=bthan ifθ=g,  allowing markets to clear and
32:1233:63910:22:21:72:258:599:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sustaining a low-price equilibrium.
32:1234:63945:21:22:89:539:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Conversely, suppose that the common price is high and that the short-sale constraint
32:1235:64029:22:22:72:540:556:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:binds on the informed.  Observing a high price, uninformed investors now infer that the
32:1236:64116:22:21:72:540:534:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bond  is  likely  to  be  of  high  quality,  boosting  their  demand.   Since  informed  investors
32:1237:64215:21:22:72:540:513:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:do not participate, however, this is entirely consistent with market-clearing.  Intuitively,
32:1238:64307:22:22:72:540:491:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:short-sale constraints may thus prevent the information held by informed investors from
32:1239:64394:22:27:72:493:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:being impounded into prices, allowing the model to sustain multiple equilibria.

33:1307:66955:151:22:89:539:269:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Taken together, the figures show that multiplicity is partly sustained by both jumps
33:1308:67039:22:22:72:540:247:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in the price schedule and in the set of states for which prices overlap,  so as to ensure
33:1309:67128:22:21:72:540:225:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:market-clearing in all states. The logic underlying multiplicity (and also non-existence of
33:1310:67219:21:22:72:540:204:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equilibrium) in our model is thus similar to the one that pervades competitive equilibria
33:1311:67308:22:22:72:540:182:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with heterogeneous information more generally:  prices are determined by local beliefs,
33:1312:67395:22:19:72:540:160:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:but these can jump discontinuously while being consistent with optimality and updating.
33:1313:67482:19:15:82:539:141:7:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:14An implicit assumption maintained here is that the symmetric ignorance price schedule lies everywhere
33:1314:67585:15:12:72:539:126:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:above the threshold1−κbbelow which the short-sale constraint binds for informed investors givenθ=b.
33:1315:67684:12:12:72:540:114:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:This implies that it is possible for a low-quality price schedule to exist that does not require jumps in the
33:1316:67793:12:12:72:540:102:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:region of overlap in order to get informed investors to bid on low-quality bonds. Parameters may be such
33:1317:67897:12:12:72:539:90:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:that this is not feasible for sufficiently lown, however. In this case, there is no equilibrium with a continuous
33:1318:68010:12:0:72:294:78:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:low-quality price schedule in the range of overlap.

34:1320:68142:53:35:72:447:655:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:5    Characterization of DP Auction Equilibrium
34:1321:68189:35:21:72:540:620:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We now characterize discriminatory-price auctions, and usePDP(s;n)to denote the price
34:1322:68274:21:22:72:540:599:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f10:B:for each state and eachnin the discriminatory protocol.  Similarly, will useBDP,U(s;n)
34:1323:68360:22:22:71:539:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for the bids of the uninformed andBDP,I(s,θ;n)for the bids of the informed.  Whenever
34:1324:68445:22:21:71:540:555:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:there is no risk of confusion, we use the simpler notationP(s),BU(s), andBI(s,θ).  As
34:1325:68530:21:45:71:416:534:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:before, we start with the symmetric benchmarksn= 0andn= 1.

35:1443:70537:39:22:89:539:312:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:As in the UP auction, the benefit of being informed when all other investors are unin-

35:1447:70883:22:40:71:245:225:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:contingent on the state, however.
35:1448:70916:40:30:71:235:185:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:5.1.2    Symmetric Information
35:1449:70946:30:22:71:539:155:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:With symmetric information (n= 1), we can again separately construct the equilibrium
35:1450:71030:22:21:71:539:133:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for eachθ. All equilibrium conditions are the same as in the symmetric ignorance case, ex-
35:1451:71120:21:0:71:539:112:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cept that investors useκθ(s)rather thanκUto evaluate their first-order conditions. Hence
36:1452:71210:0:40:72:269:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the system of first-order conditions is
36:1453:71249:40:0:96:117:668:12:g_d0_f9:8:g_d0_f16:A:−U′

36:1457:71261:13:0:202:273:668:12:g_d0_f9:8:g_d0_f16:?:·~P·κθ(s)+U′

36:1460:71286:0:13:376:383:681:12:g_d0_f14:12:g_d0_f14:A:)

36:1462:71288:0:13:392:398:681:12:g_d0_f14:12:g_d0_f14:C:[

36:1465:71294:13:39:435:515:668:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f7:A:·[1−κθ(s)] = 0.
36:1466:71309:39:30:71:269:629:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:5.1.3    No replication in DP auctions
36:1467:71347:30:22:71:539:599:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In contrast to the UP auction, information is valuable in a DP auction even ifallinvestors
36:1468:71437:22:21:71:539:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are informed and prices are fully revealing ex-post.  The reason is that bids are executed
36:1469:71527:21:22:71:539:556:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:at the bid price. Hence uninformed investors will typically pay higher prices than the in-
36:1470:71617:22:22:71:539:534:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:formed even if they buy the same number of bonds in a given state. DP auctions thus of-
36:1471:71704:22:21:71:539:512:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:fer a stark contrast to general equilibrium models with asymmetric information, in which
36:1472:71792:21:22:71:539:491:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the value of information is zero when prices are fully revealing ex-post.  The following
36:1473:71880:22:22:71:539:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:proposition formalizes this argument under mild regularity conditions. We then provide
36:1474:71966:22:25:71:268:447:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:an example to clarify the mechanism.
36:1475:72002:25:26:71:370:422:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f6:C:Proposition 10.Replication is not feasible in a DP auction if
36:1476:72063:26:30:86:314:396:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:A:1.κg6=κbandf(g)andf(b)are both positive.
36:1477:72103:30:25:86:533:366:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f7:A:2.  the informed investor bids positive amounts for bothθ=gandθ=bfor some values ofη.
36:1478:72188:25:22:72:539:341:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f6:F:Example 1.Consider an equilibrium in which all investors are informed. Assume that parameters
36:1479:72281:22:22:72:540:319:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:are such that equilibrium prices differ across quality shocks at the smallest possible demand shock,
36:1480:72381:22:21:72:540:297:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f10:F:P(g,0)> P(b,0), and that informed investors bid positive quantities at both prices,BI(θ,0)>0
36:1481:72473:21:22:71:540:276:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:for allθ. (It is trivial to choose parameters such that these assumptions are satisfied). Suppose now
36:1482:72574:22:22:71:539:254:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:that uninformed investors want to replicate the informed portfolio. Since an uninformed investor’s
36:1483:72672:22:21:71:540:232:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:bids at the high price are accepted in both states, he spendsP(g,0)BU([g,0]) +P(b,0)BU([b,0]),
36:1484:72766:21:22:72:540:211:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f10:F:while an informed investor spendsP(b,0)BI([b,0]).   Hence even ifBU([g,0]) +BU([b,0])  =
36:1485:72854:22:22:72:539:189:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f6:F:BI([b,0])and both investors buy the same quantity of risky bonds in state(g,0), the uninformed
36:1486:72948:22:44:72:405:167:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:C:investor pays more and thus has fewer risk-free bonds in his portfolio.
36:1487:73019:44:30:72:506:123:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:5.2    Asymmetric Information – Special Case with Log Preferences
36:1488:73084:30:21:72:540:93:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We now return to the special case with log preferences to study equilibrium prices under
36:1489:73172:21:0:72:540:72:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:asymmetric information,n∈(0,1)) Given the discrete grid for demand shockη∈ H,
