37:1598:73922:39:22:72:540:310:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The joint solution to these systems of first-order necessary conditions converges arbitrar-
37:1599:74013:22:22:72:539:288:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ily closely to the solution under continuous demand shocks asHbecomes arbitrarily fine.
37:1600:74100:22:21:72:540:266:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(Of course, the linear algebra conditions will become infinite dimensional in the limit).
37:1601:74189:21:32:72:502:245:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:They also highlight the fourth important difference between UP and DP auctions.
37:1602:74268:32:22:72:540:213:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f6:F:Remark 6.Consider an uninformed investor bidding ̄Bat some marginal price ̄P. In a UP auc-
37:1603:74358:22:21:72:540:191:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:tion, the investor is concerned with inferring the default probability-weighted marginal utilities
37:1604:74456:21:22:72:539:170:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:associated with state giving rise to marginal price ̄P. In a DP auction, the investor is instead con-
37:1605:74557:22:22:72:539:148:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f13:F:cerned with inferring the default probability (and the cumulated marginal utilities) of theentire
37:1606:74654:22:0:72:461:126:12:g_d0_f13:12:g_d0_f23:C:set of statesin which( ̄B, ̄P)is in the money.  That is, the investor must inferE
37:1607:74735:0:10:463:470:136:12:g_d0_f14:12:g_d0_f14:C:{
37:1608:74736:10:0:470:531:126:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f7:C: ̃κ(P)|P≤ ̄P
37:1609:74748:0:31:533:540:136:12:g_d0_f14:12:g_d0_f14:C:}
37:1610:74749:31:22:72:540:105:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:and the associated cumulation of marginal utilities, because the marginal utility from increasing a
37:1611:74848:22:0:72:401:83:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:C:given bid is evaluated at the bid price rather than the marginal price.
38:1612:74921:0:22:89:539:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Solving for equilibrium prices in DP auctions with asymmetric information is analyt-
38:1613:75005:22:22:72:540:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ically intractable.  Hence we use our numerical example from Table 1 to illustrate prices
38:1614:75094:22:21:72:200:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and comparative statics.
38:1615:75118:21:22:89:539:643:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f10:A:We first compute the equilibrium in the benchmarks with symmetric information (n=
38:1616:75199:22:22:72:540:621:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f3:B:1) and symmetric ignorance (n= 0).  As before, we consider two values for the ex-ante
38:1617:75284:22:21:72:539:599:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:probability of the bad state,f(b)∈ {0.25,0.5}.   The price functions are in Panel (a) of
38:1618:75372:21:22:72:540:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Figure  5.   As  with  the  UP  auction,  the  price  schedules  are  independent  off(b)under
38:1619:75466:22:22:72:539:556:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:symmetric information, but they depend onf(b)under symmetric ignorance. The graph
38:1620:75547:22:21:72:539:534:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:shows that, asf(b)decreases, the badθ-state is less likely and the price schedule under
38:1621:75634:21:22:72:540:513:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:symmetric ignorance (in black) gradually increases from the fully informed low-quality
38:1622:75720:22:22:72:501:491:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:price schedule (in red) to the fully informed high-quality price schedule (in blue).
38:1623:75804:22:21:89:539:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:More generally, the benchmark price schedules look similar in terms of both shape and
38:1624:75889:21:22:72:540:448:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:level to their UP analogs in Panel (a) of Figure 2. This is not a coincidence: in Appendix B
38:1625:75981:22:22:72:540:426:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:we show formally that average prices are indeed the same in the symmetric benchmarks.
38:1626:76066:22:21:72:540:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:To highlight the similarities UP and the DP auctions at the symmetric information bench-
38:1627:76154:21:22:72:540:383:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:marks, Panel (b) of Figure 5 shows marginal prices and bid functions forn= 0.  (Notice
38:1628:76240:22:22:72:540:361:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the change in scale relative to Panel (a)). Since there is price dispersion in the DP auction,
38:1629:76334:22:21:72:539:339:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:we also plot theaverage pricein the DP auction for each value of the supply shockψin
38:1630:76418:21:22:72:540:318:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:solid black. The average price schedule is flatter than the marginal price schedule because
38:1631:76509:22:22:72:540:296:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the latter is strictly decreasing.  In the UP auction, there is no price dispersion and so av-
38:1632:76603:22:21:72:539:274:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:erage and marginal prices coincide (plotted in red).15By construction, if the average price
38:1633:76694:21:22:72:540:253:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in the DP auction is the same as the average price in the UP auction, then total bids per
38:1634:76783:22:22:72:540:231:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:investor are also the same.  At the same time, the average price schedule is flatter in DP
38:1635:76873:22:22:72:540:209:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:auctions because a fraction of bids are locked in at high prices. Hence low marginal prices
38:1636:76964:22:21:72:540:187:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:apply only to the residual bids needed to cover any additional demand shocks, while low
38:1637:77051:21:22:72:327:166:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:marginal prices apply toallbids in UP auctions.
38:1638:77098:22:22:89:540:144:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The marginal price in the UP auction when all investors participate (that is,ψ=  1)
38:1639:77181:22:19:72:540:122:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is higher than in the DP auction because bidders are willing to bid more aggressively
38:1640:77266:19:15:82:540:103:7:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:15The average and marginal prices in the DP auction also coincide atψ= 1since there is no price disper-
38:1641:77369:15:0:72:340:88:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:sion in this case. Hence there is price dispersion for allψ6= 1.

40:1731:79640:21:22:89:539:221:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Observe first that the spread between the high-quality and low-quality price sched-

40:1733:79818:22:21:72:540:177:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:adverse selection problem:  if they bid on the high-quality schedule,  they will overpay
40:1734:79906:21:22:72:540:156:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in the bad state since the government is sure to accept their high-state bids and executes
40:1735:79996:22:22:72:539:134:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:them at the bid price.  Fornsufficiently large (n= 0.6in our example), the uninformed
40:1736:80081:22:21:72:540:112:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:may therefore refrain from placing any bids on the high-price schedule. This has two ef-
40:1737:80169:21:0:72:540:91:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:fects. First, the an uninformed investors who bids only on the low-price schedule knows
41:1738:80258:0:22:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that,conditionalon a bid being accepted, the state must be bad.  Hence they choose the
41:1739:80344:22:22:71:539:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:same portfolio as informed investors whenθ=b, and the low-quality schedule is locally
41:1740:80429:22:21:71:540:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:independent ofn.  Second, precisely because the uninformed do not participate at high
41:1741:80514:21:22:71:539:643:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:prices, informed investors have to buy more bonds per capita in the good state, and are
41:1742:80601:22:22:71:539:621:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:therefore disproportionately exposed to the government’s default risk.   Since there are
41:1743:80689:22:21:71:540:599:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:fewer participants asndecreases (above and beyond the lack of participation generated
41:1744:80774:21:22:71:370:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:by the demand shock), the high-price schedule must fall.
41:1745:80830:22:22:89:539:556:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Whennis sufficiently small (n= 0.4in our example), prices on the high-quality sched-
41:1746:80914:22:21:71:539:534:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ule are low enough such that the uninformed investors are less worried about adverse
41:1747:80998:21:22:71:539:513:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:selection and begin to bid on both price schedules. Since bids on the high-price schedule
41:1748:81087:22:22:71:539:491:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are also executed in the bad state, there is less residual demand that needs to be met by
41:1749:81176:22:21:71:476:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:marginal bids on the low-price schedule. Hence the low-price schedule rises.
41:1750:81252:21:22:89:540:448:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f10:A:The adverse selection effect continues to operate asndecreases further (ton=  0.1

41:1752:81430:22:21:71:540:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:below those of the informed on the high-price schedule, reductions inncontinue to fur-
41:1753:81516:21:22:72:540:383:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ther concentrate default risk in informed portfolios.   This forces a large fraction of the
41:1754:81607:22:22:72:539:361:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:high-quality schedule to drop below theuninformedprice schedule. That is, the adverse
41:1755:81692:22:21:72:540:339:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:selection effect may be severe enough that prices are lower than in the uninformed equi-
41:1756:81780:21:22:72:540:318:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f10:B:librium conditional on bad newsandgood news. Finally, whennis very small (n= 0.02
41:1757:81861:22:22:72:540:296:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in the figure), price schedules start overlapping.  Uninformed investors are now willing
41:1758:81949:22:21:72:540:274:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to participate fully on both schedules, and, as the next result shows, prices converge to
41:1759:82038:21:32:72:285:253:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the uninformed price schedule asn→0.

41:1761:82158:31:32:72:434:190:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f3:B:Proof.The proof of the analogous statement in Proposition 9 applies.
41:1762:82226:32:21:72:540:158:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f6:F:Remark 7.Despite the fact that bid overhang never binds in DP auction,  it is  instructive  to
41:1763:82320:21:22:71:539:137:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:revisit its role in our auction model here.  Specifically, once the uninformed start bidding on the
41:1764:82419:22:22:71:539:115:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:high-quality  schedule,  their  overhanging  bids  impact  the  equilibrium  prices  at  the  low-quality
41:1765:82524:22:21:71:539:93:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:schedule in a manner reminiscent of the way the bid-overhang constraint affected the UP auction:
41:1766:82620:21:0:71:539:72:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:they drag up the prices on the low-quality schedule by forcing the execution of some high-price bids
42:1767:82722:0:22:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:originally intended for a different state. Nevertheless, the mechanism is quite different, because the
42:1768:82824:22:22:72:540:686:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:uninformed investors’ accumulated bids reduce the available supply of bonds for the informed and
42:1769:82920:22:21:72:540:664:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:thereby raise prices.   Another key difference is while the bid-overhang constraint restricted the
42:1770:83018:21:22:72:540:643:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:set of equilibria in the UP auction, in DP auctions the overhanging bids act on the nature of the
42:1771:83115:22:22:72:540:621:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:equilibrium.  The bid-overhang does not induce a pooling of prices as the inference is not at each
42:1772:83213:22:21:72:540:599:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:price but instead in-the-money set.  The bid-overhang operates as soon as uninformed investors
42:1773:83307:21:22:72:539:578:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:start bidding at prices in the high-quality schedule (around0.4in the example) and not when
42:1774:83398:22:22:72:539:556:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:they become the marginal investor (atn=ηMas in the UP auction example).  Even though the
42:1775:83486:22:21:72:540:534:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:bid-overhang constraint operates differently in both protocols, it remains the force that guarantees
42:1776:83586:21:40:72:304:513:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:C:convergence of price schedules in both asn→0.
42:1777:83631:40:30:72:322:473:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f10:C:5.2.2    Comparative statics with respect tof(b)
42:1778:83679:30:22:72:540:443:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:What if a government’s quality improves and the probability that a country is in the bad
42:1779:83767:22:22:72:539:421:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:state,f(b), declines?  Interestingly, there is not much effect when a large number of in-
42:1780:83856:22:21:72:540:399:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:vestors are informed.  In the UP auction, there is perfect replication whenn > ηM(the
42:1781:83941:21:22:72:539:378:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bid-overhang not binding) and the two schedules are independent onf(b)conditional on
42:1782:84025:22:22:72:540:356:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:B:θ.  In the DP auction,conditionalon the uninformed not participating on the high-quality
42:1783:84113:22:21:72:539:334:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:schedule, prices are also independent off(b).  The probability of a bad bondf(b), how-
42:1784:84199:21:22:72:539:313:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ever, changes the ex-ante expected probability of defaultκU, which is critical in determin-
42:1785:84290:22:22:72:540:291:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ing the symmetric ignorance schedule towards which prices converge asn→0.  Indeed,
42:1786:84372:22:21:72:539:269:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:once the bid-overhang constraint operates, at relatively lown, the parameterf(b)does af-
42:1787:84460:21:22:72:540:248:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:fect prices. In the UP auction, the point at which the bid-overhang constraint binds is just
42:1788:84552:22:22:72:539:226:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:B:ηM, independent off(b).  Conditional on binding,f(b)affects the inference problem and
42:1789:84637:22:21:72:539:204:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:thus the shape of the overlapping price schedules. In the DP auction, a lowerf(b)also re-
42:1790:84726:21:22:72:540:183:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:duces the likelihood that the uninformed buys an overpriced bad bond, speeding up and
42:1791:84811:22:22:72:540:161:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:increasing the participation of the uninformed on the high-quality schedule. This in turn
42:1792:84900:22:21:72:539:139:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:implies that the low price schedule begins to rise for higher values ofn.  Contrary to the
42:1793:84990:21:22:72:540:118:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:UP auction, the point at which the bid-overhang constraint operates thus does depend on
42:1794:85077:22:0:72:330:96:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:B:f(b). This is summarized in the next proposition.
43:1795:85128:0:40:72:435:707:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:6    Comparison Between UP and DP Protocols
43:1796:85171:40:30:72:365:667:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:6.1    Level and Volatility of Sovereign Yields
43:1797:85218:30:21:72:540:637:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We  now  examine  the  implications  of  the  choice  auction  protocol  from  the  perspective
43:1798:85313:21:22:72:540:616:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of the government for different values ofn.  Rather than explicitly specifying a govern-
43:1799:85401:22:22:71:539:594:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ment payoff function, we simply assume that the government (i) prefers to sell bonds at
43:1800:85488:22:21:71:539:572:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:high prices (or equivalently, low yields), and (ii) dislikes price volatility stemming from
43:1801:85579:21:22:71:336:551:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:demand shocks, since these are outside its control.
43:1802:85630:22:40:89:511:529:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The yield on a govenrment bond sold at pricePis equal to the promised return,
43:1803:85707:40:0:266:307:489:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f10:C:Y ield=
43:1804:85714:0:16:311:340:497:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f7:C:1−P
43:1805:85717:16:0:321:329:481:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:C:P
43:1806:85718:0:39:342:345:489:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:C:.
43:1807:85719:39:22:71:539:450:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In UP auctions, all bonds are sold at the same price, and we can simply compute the equi-
43:1808:85808:22:22:71:539:428:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:librium yield using the unique marginal price.  In DP auctions, we compute a quantity-
43:1809:85894:22:21:71:539:406:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:weighted average yield using the individual yields on all sold bonds. This average yield
43:1810:85982:21:22:71:539:385:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:captures the risk-neutral component of the government’s payoff.  Note that the govern-
43:1811:86068:22:22:71:539:363:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ment’s debt burden can be defined asD/P=D(1 +Y ield). Hence the government faces
43:1812:86148:22:21:71:440:341:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a higher average debt burden if bonds trade at a higher average yield.
43:1813:86218:21:22:89:539:320:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The risky component of the government’s payoff is given by the variation in the aver-
43:1814:86303:22:22:71:539:298:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:age yield conditional on the quality of the bond, and captures the government’s exposure
43:1815:86391:22:21:71:539:276:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to demand shocks.16Figure 7 plots average yield (the risk-neutral component) and its
43:1816:86475:21:22:71:484:255:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:average conditional variance (the risky component) for both types of auctions.
43:1817:86553:22:22:89:539:233:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f10:A:Compare first the benchmarks of symmetric information (n= 1) and ignorance (n=
43:1818:86631:22:21:72:539:211:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f3:B:0).  Given that average prices and total bids are the same across auction protocols under
43:1819:86720:21:22:72:540:190:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:symmetry,  so are average yields.   The average conditional variance of the yield,  while
43:1820:86809:22:19:72:540:168:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:small in both cases, is substantially lower in the DP auction, however.  As we discussed
43:1821:86897:19:16:82:539:149:7:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:16There is also an ex-ante variance across quality bonds. Because we have made the default probabilities
43:1822:87001:16:12:72:540:133:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:so different in order to allow for perfect replication in the UP auction, the differences across quality shocks
43:1823:87112:12:11:72:540:121:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:swamp the conditional variance in our numerical example.  However, this would not be true when these
43:1824:87212:11:12:72:540:110:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:differences  were  smaller.   For  example,  iff(g)→0,  almost  all  bond  yield  volatility  is  due  to  demand
43:1825:87325:12:12:71:539:98:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:shocks rather than quality shocks. For this reason, we have chosen to focus on the behavior of the average
43:1826:87431:12:0:71:163:86:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:conditional variance.

44:1868:87957:188:22:72:540:454:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:when describing Figure 5, this is because the lion’s share of bids in a DP auction is exe-
44:1869:88047:22:22:72:540:432:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cuted at the highest state-contigent price. Specifically, yield volatility is determined by the
44:1870:88142:22:21:72:539:410:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:slope of price schedules conditional on aθ-state, and these are flatter in DP auctions. The
44:1871:88233:21:22:72:527:389:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:average yield is lower under symmetric ignorance than under symmetric information.
44:1872:88315:22:22:89:539:367:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Next turn to asymmetric information,n∈(0,1).  The behavior of yields and condi-
44:1873:88394:22:21:72:540:345:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tional variances now differs qualitatively across protocols.  In UP auctions, the average
44:1874:88483:21:22:72:540:324:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:yield rises monotonically until the point of perfect replication, and is constant thereafter
44:1875:88575:22:22:72:539:302:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as the equilibrium becomes invariant with respect ton.  In contrast, the average condi-
44:1876:88662:22:21:72:540:280:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tional variance of the yield shows a strong non-monotonicity in the region in which the
44:1877:88749:21:22:72:540:259:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bid-overhang constraint binds. The reason is that the bid-overhang constraint forces price
44:1878:88839:22:22:72:539:237:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:pooling, thereby steepening the slope of overlapping price schedules asngrows.  Steep
44:1879:88924:22:21:72:519:215:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:price schedules imply that equilibrium prices are highly sensitive to demand shocks.
44:1880:89008:21:22:89:539:194:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In DP auctions, the average yield is hump-shaped, increasing for low levels ofnand
44:1881:89090:22:22:72:539:172:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:declining for high levels ofn. Ifnis low, uninformed investors bid on both schedules, but
44:1882:89179:22:21:72:540:150:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:face adverse selection because bid on the high-quality schedule are also accepted in the
44:1883:89267:21:22:72:540:129:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bad state. This depresses prices on the high-quality schedule to an extent that is not fully
44:1884:89359:22:22:72:539:107:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f13:B:compensated by an increase of the low-quality schedule.  Indeed, theadverse selection
44:1885:89444:22:0:72:539:85:12:g_d0_f13:12:g_d0_f3:B:effectgrows in importance asnrises, up to the point where uninformed investor stop
45:1886:89528:0:22:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bidding on the high-quality schedule. When only informed investors participate, further
45:1887:89615:22:22:72:540:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:increases innlead to lower per-capita risk exposure.   As a result,  informed investors’
45:1888:89703:22:21:72:539:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:information rents are gradually competed away asngrows.  (Bad-state prices are unaf-
45:1889:89787:21:22:72:540:643:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:fected because the uninformed choose the same portfolio as the informed conditional on
45:1890:89873:22:22:72:540:621:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the bad state.)  Thiscannibalization effectraises prices in the good state and reduces the
45:1891:89963:22:21:72:540:599:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:yield asn→1. In contrast to UP auctions, the conditional variance is small for alln. The
45:1892:90051:21:22:72:540:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reason again is that the lion’s share of expenditures is made at the highest bid price. Large
45:1893:90144:22:22:72:540:556:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:demand shocks thus necessitate only a marginal price adjustment.  Furthermore, the ab-
45:1894:90230:22:21:72:540:534:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sence of the bid-overhang constraint means that price schedules need not be as steep as
45:1895:90317:21:22:72:385:513:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in a UP auction, reducing the sensitivity to demand shocks.
45:1896:90376:22:22:89:539:491:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The choice of auction protocol thus leads to arisk-return tradeoffbetween average
45:1897:90457:22:21:72:540:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:yields and volatility for the government. When information is symmetric, both protocols
45:1898:90544:21:22:72:540:448:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:deliver the same average prices, but DP auctions offer lower exposure to demand shocks.
45:1899:90631:22:22:72:540:426:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Whennis relatively low, average yields are similar (and increasing inn), but UP protocols
45:1900:90720:22:21:72:539:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:feature more exposure to demand shocks. Whennis relatively large (in particular, when
45:1901:90805:21:22:72:540:383:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:B:nis such that the UP auction allows for perfect replication), the UP auction still displays
45:1902:90896:22:22:72:540:361:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a larger conditional variance, but a smaller average yield.  The resolution of this tradeoff
45:1903:90988:22:21:72:509:339:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:depends on the government’s preferences for lower average yields versus volatiliy.
45:1904:91070:21:22:89:539:318:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Note that Figure 7 shows average yields and conditional variances for two different
45:1905:91153:22:22:72:540:296:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:values off(b).  When the ex-ante probability that the bond is of low quality is smaller
45:1906:91240:22:21:72:540:274:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(f(b)  =  0.25instead off(b)  =  0.5), average yields and volatility falls for alln.  This is
45:1907:91333:21:22:72:540:253:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:quite natural as the bond is less likely to default. More interestingly, the peak in average
45:1908:91425:22:22:72:539:231:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:yields in DP auctions occurs for highernwhenf(b)is lower. This is because uninformed
45:1909:91509:22:22:72:540:209:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:investors are less afraid of bidding on the hiqh-quality schedule because the risk of over-
45:1910:91600:22:21:72:540:187:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:paying  in  the  bad  state  is  lower.   Hence  they  continue  participating  in  both  states  for
45:1911:91701:21:22:72:539:166:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:relatively high values ofn.   In the figure,  the peak in average yields occurs at around
45:1912:91790:22:0:72:404:144:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:B:n= 0.5whenf(b) = 0.5and aroundn= 0.75whenf(b) = 0.25.

46:1938:92596:188:21:89:539:353:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In the benchmark symmetric ignorance case, the utility levels obtained by informed
46:1939:92678:21:22:72:540:332:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and uninformed investors, respectively, are the same in both protocols.  This is because
46:1940:92766:22:22:72:540:310:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:prices are not contingent onθatn=  0,  and so there are no price differences that can
46:1941:92851:22:21:72:540:288:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:be differentially exploited across protocols by an atomistic informed investors.   This is
46:1942:92941:21:22:72:539:267:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:not the case in the symmetric information benchmark (n= 1), however. While informed
46:1943:93024:22:22:72:540:245:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:investors obtain the same payoffs in both protocols, the uninformed payoff is substan-
46:1944:93110:22:21:72:540:223:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tially different. In the UP auction, informed investors can perfectly replicate the informed
46:1945:93202:21:22:72:540:202:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:portfolio, and they thus obtain the same same payoff as well.  In the DP auction, perfect
46:1946:93291:22:22:72:540:180:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:replication is not attainable because the uninformed would pay higher prices in the bad
46:1947:93378:22:21:72:533:158:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:state. Hence they earn achieve lower utility than uninformed investors in a UP auction.
46:1948:93465:21:22:89:539:137:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:When information is asymmetric, the comparative statics of both informed and un-
46:1949:93545:22:22:72:539:115:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:informed investor utlity with respect tonare qualitatively different across auction pro-
46:1950:93633:22:21:71:539:93:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tocols.  First, consider uninformed investors.  In a UP auction, uninformed utility is in-
46:1951:93723:21:0:71:539:72:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:creasing innbecause (partial) portfolio replication allows the uninformed to free ride
47:1952:93811:0:22:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on the information impounded into prices by informed investors, of which there is more
47:1953:93897:22:22:72:540:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:when there are more informed investors. In a DP auction, instead, the degree of adverse
47:1954:93984:22:21:72:399:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:selection is increasing inn, and hence so is uninformed utility.
47:1955:94048:21:22:89:539:643:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Next, consider informed investors.  In a UP auction, all investors pay the same price.
47:1956:94134:22:22:71:539:621:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Since informed investors bid more aggressively than uninformed investors on average,
47:1957:94218:22:21:71:539:599:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:an increase innraises prices and lowers rents. Hence informed investor utility is decreas-
47:1958:94308:21:22:71:539:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ing innuntiln=ηM. (Beyond this point, uninformed investors can perfectly replication
47:1959:94392:22:22:72:539:556:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and payoffs are invariant ton.)  In a DP auction, bids are executed at the bid price, and
47:1960:94481:22:21:72:540:534:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f7:B:uninformed investors face adverse selection.  Ifnis small to begin with, increases inn
47:1961:94567:21:22:71:539:513:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:increase the severity of adverse selection, and uninformed investors participate less and
47:1962:94656:22:22:71:539:491:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:less. This reduced participation lowers prices on average, leading to an increase in infra-
47:1963:94747:22:21:71:539:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:marginal rents and utility earned by informed investors. Once we reach the point where
47:1964:94833:21:22:71:539:448:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the uninformed no longer participate on the high-state schedule, the comparative static
47:1965:94920:22:22:71:539:426:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reverses.  Now, further increases innjust serve to increase competition for bonds in the
47:1966:95008:22:21:71:539:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:high-state, leading to price increases that erode information rents.  (The utility level ob-
47:1967:95100:21:22:71:539:383:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tained in the low state is constant, since both informed and uninformed investor choose
47:1968:95187:22:22:71:539:361:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the same portfolio.)  Importantly, the value of information is strictly positive even in the
47:1969:95279:22:21:71:345:339:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:limitn→1where prices are fully revealing ex-post.
47:1970:95328:21:22:89:539:318:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The figure also shows the comparison between two different levels off(b).  A lower
47:1971:95410:22:22:71:539:296:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:probability  of  the  bad  state  increases  marginal  prices,  leading  to  lower  infra-marginal
47:1972:95508:22:21:71:540:274:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rents  on  all  bond  purchases.   Hence  investors  are  worse  off  iff(b)  =  0.25.   While  the
47:1973:95607:21:22:72:540:253:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f10:B:effect off(b)just scales down prices for eachnin the UP auction (as we discussedf(b)
47:1974:95691:22:22:72:540:231:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:does not change the point at which the bid-overhang constraint binds in UP auctions), in
47:1975:95779:22:22:72:540:209:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:DP auctions a lowerf(b)implies that uninformed participate earlier in the high-quality
47:1976:95865:22:21:72:540:187:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:schedule, generating a different non-monotonicity in informed utility.  Lastly, note that
47:1977:95954:21:22:72:540:166:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the  cost  of  not  participating  in  the  high-state  for  the  uninformed  in  a  DP  auction  are
47:1978:96055:22:22:72:540:144:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:higher when the probability of being in the good state is high,  even in the benchmark
47:1979:96141:22:21:72:539:122:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:withn= 1.  (That is, the payoffs decline more for the uninformed than for the informed
47:1980:96227:21:0:72:296:101:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in the symmetric information benchmark).
48:1981:96269:0:31:72:321:708:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:6.2.1    Endogenizing Information Acquisition
48:1982:96314:31:21:72:540:677:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We now endogenize the share of informed investorsnby allowing for information ac-
48:1983:96395:21:22:72:540:656:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:quisition.  All investors are initially uninformed.  After learning whether they will make
48:1984:96485:22:22:72:540:634:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:it to the auction (that is, after learning whether they were hit by the demand shock), in-
48:1985:96575:22:21:72:539:612:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:vestors can learn the true value ofθby paying autility costofK.  An investor chooses
48:1986:96659:21:22:71:539:591:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to become informed if the value of information exceeds its cost, and will remain unin-
48:1987:96745:22:22:71:539:569:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:formed otherwise. Denote byVU(n)the expected utility of an uninformed investor given
48:1988:96829:22:21:71:540:547:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:B:n(see Equation 1), and byVI(n)the expected utility of an informed investor givenn(see
48:1989:96914:21:22:71:539:526:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Equation 6).  The dependence onnreflects the fact that equilibrium prices will depend
48:1990:96999:22:22:71:539:504:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on the share of informed investors, as shown in Figure 8.  Then the following optimality
48:1991:97087:22:39:71:321:482:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f7:B:conditions determine the equilibrium level ofn
48:1992:97133:39:25:224:540:443:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:A:VI(n)−K≥VU(n)ifn >0(21)
48:1993:97156:25:39:224:540:418:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:A:VI(n)−K≤VU(n)ifn <1.(22)
48:1994:97180:39:22:71:540:379:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In an interior equilibrium withn∈(0,1), both conditions must simultaneously hold with
48:1995:97265:22:32:71:470:357:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equality. An equilibrium with information acquisition is defined as follows.
48:1996:97341:32:21:71:540:325:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f6:F:Definition 9.For both the UP and DP auctions, an equilibrium of the model with endogenous
48:1997:97430:21:22:71:540:304:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:information acquisition consists of the measure of informed tradersn∗, a price scheduleP(s),a bid
48:1998:97527:22:22:71:539:282:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:schedule for the uninformedBU(s),and a bid schedule for the informedBI(s,θ).The bid schedules
48:1999:97620:22:21:71:540:260:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:must be solutions to the investors’ problems givenPand satisfy the short-sale constraints.  The
48:2000:97715:21:22:71:539:239:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:F:bids and price schedules must satisfy the debt-overhang constraints and auction clearing for all
48:2001:97811:22:32:71:459:217:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f6:C:(θ,η), andn∗must satisfy the information acquisition criterion in(21)and(22).
48:2002:97888:32:21:89:539:185:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Given that investors are ex-ante identical, the value of information is simply the differ-
48:2003:97978:21:22:72:540:164:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ence in expected utility obtained by informed and uninformed investors,VI(n)−VU(n).
48:2004:98061:22:22:72:539:142:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We show thispayoff gapin Figure 9. There are large differences across auction protocols,
48:2005:98149:22:21:72:540:120:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:which has important consequences for equilibrium information acquisition.  Specifically,
48:2006:98237:21:22:72:540:99:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the equilibrium share of informed investorsn∗is determined by equalizing the payoff
48:2007:98320:22:0:72:302:77:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:gap and the information acquisition costK.

49:2034:98790:196:22:89:539:454:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Figure 9 has certain features which numerical exploration suggests are common to
49:2035:98870:22:21:72:540:432:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:this class of models.  If we letn∗prdenote the equilibrium share of informed investors in

49:2046:99584:21:31:101:143:146:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f3:A:∀K >0.
49:2047:99590:31:22:72:540:115:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The fact that there are fewer informed with UP auctions does not mean that there is less
49:2048:99678:22:21:72:540:93:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:information in prices.  In our baseline example, whenf(b) = 0.5, thenK= 0.041(which
49:2049:99761:21:0:72:540:72:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is the value of the maximum gap in a DP auction),̂K= 0.018(which is the value of the
50:2050:99847:0:22:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:gap in both auction protocols atn= 0), andK= 0.005(which is the value of the gap for
50:2051:99931:22:39:72:187:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:DP auctions atn= 1).
50:2052:99951:39:30:72:366:647:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:6.2.2    Relationship with Grossman and Stiglitz (1980)
50:2053:100006:30:22:72:540:617:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:A classical question in general equilibrium theory pertains to where the information con-
50:2054:100095:22:21:72:540:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tained in prices comes from.  Grossman and Stiglitz (1980) argued that price-taking in-
50:2055:100182:21:22:72:540:574:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:vestors have no incentive to look at or acquire their private information if this informa-
50:2056:100272:22:22:72:540:552:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tion is already encapsulated in the price. But if their demands do not reflect their private
50:2057:100364:22:21:72:540:530:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:information, then how do prices reflect this information in the first place?  If acquiring
50:2058:100454:21:22:72:540:509:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:information is costly, this question manifests itself as a nonexistence problem known as
50:2059:100542:22:22:72:540:487:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the Grossman-Stiglitz paradox: when information is costly and prices are fully revealing,
50:2060:100631:22:21:72:540:465:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:no individual wants to acquire information.  We now discuss in detail how our auction
50:2061:100716:21:22:72:249:444:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model circumvents this difficulty.
50:2062:100750:22:22:89:539:422:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We can replicate the nonexistence problem in our UP auction if parameters are such
50:2063:100832:22:21:72:540:400:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f6:B:that  prices  are  fully  revealing  ex-post  givenn=  1andwe  simply  assume  that  the  bid-
50:2064:100926:21:22:72:540:379:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f3:B:overhang constraint does not exist. In the absence of the bid-overhang constraint, replication
50:2065:101020:22:22:72:539:357:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:atn= 1implies that replication is feasible for alln >0. Hence the value of information is
50:2066:101109:22:21:72:540:335:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:zero for alln >0, but positive forn= 0.  It follows that there is a non-existence problem
50:2067:101198:21:22:72:528:314:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:if the cost of information is strictly between zero and the value of information atn= 0.
50:2068:101286:22:22:89:539:292:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Taking into account the bid-overhang constraint, which follows endogenously from
50:2069:101366:22:21:72:540:270:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the auction protocol, eliminates this non-existence problem. Specifically, the bid-overhang
50:2070:101457:21:22:72:540:249:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:constraint hinders perfect replication for low levels ofn,  eliminating the discontinuity
50:2071:101546:22:22:72:539:227:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of information gains atn= 0, and thus inducing equilibrium existence.  Grossman and
50:2072:101629:22:21:72:540:205:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Stiglitz (1980) proposed a solution by adding a second source of noise to prevent the price
50:2073:101720:21:22:72:539:184:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:system being invertible.17In contrast we do not need to impose sufficient noise to pre-
50:2074:101807:22:22:72:540:162:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:vent prices from be fully revealing. Instead, the auction protocol forces pooling when the
50:2075:101897:22:17:72:540:140:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:fraction of informed investors is low enough, endogenously ensuring that prices are not
50:2076:101984:17:16:82:539:123:7:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:17The existence of equilibria when the shocks are continuous and hence states can have the same price
50:2077:102085:16:12:72:540:107:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:is well known to be problematic, see Allen and Jordan (1998) for a survey of the existence literature.  The
50:2078:102192:12:12:72:540:95:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:combination of CARA preferences and jointly normal shocks was key to the construction of an equilibrium
50:2079:102295:12:11:72:540:83:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:in Grossman and Stiglitz (1980), though recently Breon-Drish (2015) has developed a characterization that
50:2080:102400:11:0:72:167:72:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:drops joint normality.
51:2081:102424:0:22:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:fully revealing for any fixed level of noise. Hence an equilibrium with costly information
51:2082:102514:22:22:72:356:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:acquisition exists and lies endogenously in this range.
51:2083:102569:22:21:89:539:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The contrast is even starker in a DP auction.  In these auctions, the fact that bids are
51:2084:102657:21:22:72:540:643:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:executed at the bid price provides incentives to acquire information even when prices
51:2085:102742:22:22:72:540:621:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are  fully  revealing  ex-post.   The  fact  that  informed  investors  pay  the  correct  marginal
51:2086:102841:22:21:72:540:599:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:price in every state thus allows for informational efficiency even with costly information
51:2087:102931:21:53:72:133:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:acquisition.
51:2088:102943:53:35:72:301:525:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:7    Relationship to Literature
51:2089:102974:35:21:72:540:490:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:This paper is motivated by the complex dynamics of sovereign debt yields in primary
51:2090:103057:21:22:72:540:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:market  auctions,  particularly  in  emerging  economies.   We  have  already  discussed  the
51:2091:103150:22:22:72:540:447:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:contribution of our model to the sovereign debt literature. In this section we discuss how
51:2092:103240:22:21:72:540:425:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:our work relates three additional strands of literature. The first concerns the foundations
51:2093:103331:21:22:72:540:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of general equilibrium theory (GE) and the question of where market-clearing prices come
51:2094:103419:22:22:72:540:382:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:from. The second concerns the question of how the private information held by multiple
51:2095:103505:22:21:72:540:360:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:investors is aggregated into prices.  The third consists of auction-theoretic models with a
51:2096:103596:21:22:72:540:339:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:large number of bidders and perfectly divisible goods with uncertain common value, and
51:2097:103682:22:22:72:393:317:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the empirical application of such models to sovereign bonds.
51:2098:103742:22:21:89:539:295:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:With respect to the question of where prices come from, a key characteristic of GE the-
51:2099:103829:21:22:72:540:274:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ory is that the price vector is an endogenous object that is not chosen by anyone, yet is
51:2100:103918:22:22:72:540:252:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:determined by the accumulated actions of individuals who think of themselves as unable
51:2101:104004:22:21:72:540:230:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to affect prices. To get around this conundrum, Walras made up his fictional ”auctioneer”
51:2102:104093:21:22:72:540:209:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that matches total supply and total demand in perfectly competitive market with perfect
51:2103:104180:22:22:72:540:187:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:information and no transaction costs. But this has long been considered a thought exper-
51:2104:104268:22:21:72:540:165:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:iment that did not adequately address the basic question of prices (see Hahn (1989) for a
51:2105:104357:21:22:72:134:144:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:discussion).
51:2106:104369:22:22:89:539:122:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:One approach to endogenizing the choice of prices is the market games literature. This
51:2107:104455:22:21:72:540:100:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:literature introduces a fuller description of the environment in which all endogenous ob-
51:2108:104544:21:0:72:540:79:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:jects are selected by the agents (including prices) based upon noncooperative game the-
52:2109:104633:0:22:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ory.18Examples of this market game approach include Rubinstein and Wolinsky (1985)’s
52:2110:104717:22:22:72:540:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sequential bargaining model in which buyers and sellers are paired up under complete
52:2111:104801:22:21:72:210:664:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f3:B:information each period.19
52:2112:104827:21:22:89:539:643:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The price problem, however, becomes more severe once prices have to simultaneously
52:2113:104909:22:22:72:540:621:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:clear markets and aggregate information, as in Lucas (1972), Radner (1979) and Grossman
52:2114:104996:22:21:72:540:599:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and Stiglitz (1980).  Because agents ”need to know” both the price functionandthe real-
52:2115:105083:21:22:72:540:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ized price in order to make inferences and determine their individual demands, this leads
52:2116:105172:22:22:72:540:556:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to the complementary question of where the information in prices comes from.20The rel-
52:2117:105258:22:21:72:540:534:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:evance this question is perhaps best exemplified by the seminal work of Grossman and
52:2118:105342:21:22:72:540:513:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Stiglitz (1980), who discuss how fully revealing information prices are logically impossi-
52:2119:105432:22:22:72:91:491:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ble.
52:2120:105436:22:21:89:539:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:But  even  if  there  exists  a  fully  revealing  equilibrium,  there  is  an  implementability
52:2121:105532:21:22:72:540:448:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:problem because it may not be possible to find a trading mechanism that induces it. Kyle
52:2122:105620:22:22:72:540:426:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(1989) proposes a resolution using non-competitive rational expectations model in which
52:2123:105707:22:21:72:540:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:agents submit limit orders (or demand schedules, as in our case) taking into account their
52:2124:105797:21:22:72:540:383:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:effect on the equilibrium price. In a similar vein, Jackson (1991) proposes an environment
52:2125:105887:22:22:72:540:361:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in which the number of agents is finite and all agents internalize that the extent of infor-
52:2126:105979:22:21:72:540:339:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:mation in prices depends upon the demand schedule they submit, while Golosov, Loren-
52:2127:106063:21:22:72:540:318:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:zoni, and Tsyvinski (2014) propose a decentralized approach which features a sequence of
52:2128:106151:22:22:72:539:296:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bilateral meetings with take-it-or-leave-it offers.21Finally, Vives (2014) and Gaballo and
52:2129:106241:22:21:72:540:274:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Ordonez (2017) propose settings with large centralized markets in which the valuation of
52:2130:106329:21:22:72:540:253:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:each trader has both common and private value components, and the costly signal bun-
52:2131:106413:22:22:72:540:231:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dles information about these two components, such that prices can be fully revealing and
52:2132:106501:22:19:72:318:209:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:yet there are incentives to acquire information.
52:2133:106549:19:15:82:539:190:7:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:18See Gale (2000) for a survey of this literature and for a discussion of the alternative cooperative ap-
52:2134:106654:15:9:72:105:175:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:proach.
52:2135:106661:9:15:82:539:166:7:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:19Gale (1987) shows that these sequential bargaining models converge to a common price equilibrium as
52:2136:106762:15:9:72:213:151:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:the number of agents gets large.
52:2137:106794:9:15:82:539:142:7:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:20Dubey, Geanakoplos, and Shubik (1987) consider the Nash equilibrium of a sequential trading game
52:2138:106892:15:12:72:540:127:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:with incomplete information where traders make quantity offers to buy and sell and the price is determined
52:2139:106998:12:12:72:540:115:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:by the ratio of the total buy versus sell offers. Here information revelation occurs largely in one-step through
52:2140:107110:12:9:72:300:103:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:the vector of different prices for the different goods.
52:2141:107165:9:15:82:539:94:7:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:21A  related  contribution  is  Albagli,  Hellwig,  and  Tsyvinski  (2014)  who  develop  a  dynamic  REE  with
52:2142:107276:15:0:72:400:79:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:dispersed information in which information enters nonlinearly into prices.
53:2143:107352:0:22:89:539:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Our paper speaks to both of these problematic aspects of GE by using the structure
53:2144:107434:22:22:72:540:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of an auction to provide answer to the question of where prices come from, and under
53:2145:107518:22:21:72:540:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:what conditions there are incentives to acquire and impound information into prices even
53:2146:107606:21:22:72:540:643:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:when these are fully revealing ex-post. By specifying the auction protocol, our model fea-
53:2147:107696:22:22:72:540:621:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tures a specific order of moves.   First,  investors submit their bids (where each bid is a
53:2148:107787:22:21:72:540:599:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:price-quantity pair).  Second, a specific protocol is used to select the bids which are ac-
53:2149:107878:21:22:72:540:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cepted and the prices at which they are executed. Information revelation occurs after the
53:2150:107967:22:22:72:540:556:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:marginal price at the auction is revealed.  The information that is revealed may be com-
53:2151:108055:22:21:72:540:534:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:plete, as in REE model, but still there are incentives to acquire information because the
53:2152:108144:21:22:72:540:513:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:information is revealed only once bids can no longer be changed. A related paper which
53:2153:108230:22:22:72:540:491:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:takes an auction-based approach to micro found REE is Milgrom (1981).  He considers,
53:2154:108314:22:21:72:540:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:however, an auction in which bidders are restricted in the units they can by and where
53:2155:108400:21:22:72:540:448:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the price is not clouded by a demand (or supply) shocks. Our paper relaxes both of these
53:2156:108488:22:22:72:113:426:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:aspects.
53:2157:108496:22:21:89:539:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Our paper also contributes to the auction literature on multi-unit auctions more gen-
53:2158:108581:21:22:72:540:383:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:erally.  In contrast to the core of the auction literature, which is based on selling single
53:2159:108673:22:22:72:540:361:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:object to bidders with either independent private values22or correlated values23with a
53:2160:108759:22:21:72:540:339:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:focus on strategic bidding,  an adequate treatment of goods such as treasury bonds re-
53:2161:108845:21:22:72:540:318:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:quires extending these models multi-unit auctions. The challenge, however, is solving an
53:2162:108933:22:22:72:540:296:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equilibrium that involves bidders with a double dimensional strategic problem: choosing
53:2163:109020:22:21:72:539:274:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:both bid quantities and bid prices.24By assuming the limiting case of price taking, our set-
53:2164:109112:21:22:72:540:253:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ting allows to change the focus from bidding strategic considerations to how the auction
53:2165:109200:22:22:72:540:231:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:protocol determine prices by aggregating bids and motivating information acquisition.
53:2166:109285:22:22:72:540:209:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In single-unit auctions, Eso and White (2004) consider the interaction of ex-post risk and
53:2167:109375:22:21:72:303:187:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:auction protocols in determining bid prices.
53:2168:109419:21:22:89:539:166:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Recent work tackles these questions of how multiunit auctions determine prices in
53:2169:109500:22:19:72:540:144:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equilibrium  from  an  empirical  perspective.   Hortac ̧su  and  McAdams  (2010)  develop  a
53:2170:109593:19:12:82:483:125:7:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:?:22See Vickrey (1962), Harris and Raviv (1981), Myerson (1979) and Maskin and Riley (1985).
53:2171:109683:12:12:82:376:113:7:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:?:23See Milgrom and Weber (1982) and McAfee and McMillan (1987).
53:2172:109745:12:15:82:539:101:7:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:24See  Wilson  (1979),  Engelbrecht-Wiggans  and  Kahn  (1998),  Perry  and  Reny  (1999),  Kagel  and  Levin
53:2173:109854:15:0:72:198:86:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:(2001) and McAdams (2006).
54:2174:109882:0:22:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model based on Wilson (1979) of a multi-unit discriminatory-price auction with a finite set
54:2175:109973:22:22:72:540:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of potential risk-neutral bidders with symmetric and independent private values, using
54:2176:110059:22:21:72:540:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:data from Turkish Treasury auctions to estimate those bidders’ private values.  In their
54:2177:110147:21:22:72:540:643:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model the symmetric equilibrium bidding functions depend on how an individual bid
54:2178:110228:22:22:72:540:621:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:changes the probability distribution of the market clearing price, a complicated object to
54:2179:110318:22:21:72:540:599:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:characterize analytically. Given this theoretical difficulty, they construct a non-parametric
54:2180:110411:21:22:72:470:578:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f3:B:consistent estimator of the distribution exploiting a resampling technique.25
54:2181:110488:22:22:89:539:556:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In contrast to this empirical approach, our work is based on the presumption that bid-
54:2182:110574:22:21:71:539:534:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ders’ valuations of the auctioned treasury bonds are perfectly correlated (common value)
54:2183:110662:21:22:71:539:513:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:instead  of  independent  (private  value).   Unfortunately,  sorting  out  which  assumption
54:2184:110755:22:22:71:539:491:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is more applicable for treasury bonds is challenging.  As argued by Laffont and Vuong
54:2185:110840:22:21:71:539:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(1996), ”common value” and ”independent value” auctions are (nearly) observationally
54:2186:110924:21:22:71:539:448:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equivalent, unless there are exogenous variations that allow for identification.  As a re-
54:2187:111014:22:22:71:539:426:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sponse, Hortac ̧su and Kastl (2012) use Canadian treasury auctions to test whether com-
54:2188:111101:22:21:71:539:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:mon values or private values are a better representation of the motivations to buy treasury
54:2189:111192:21:22:71:539:383:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bonds. Even though they conclude that there is no evidence that dealers, who observe the
54:2190:111280:22:22:71:539:361:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bids of costumers, learn about fundamentals from those costumers, this is not prima fa-
54:2191:111367:22:21:71:539:339:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cie evidence that dealers follow private values, but instead that they may have superior
54:2192:111455:21:22:71:364:318:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f3:B:information than costumers about the common value.26
54:2193:111507:22:22:89:539:296:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:A second relevant difference between our approach and this empirical literature is that
54:2194:111594:22:21:71:539:274:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:we assume investors are risk averse, not risk neutral. This departure is not only relevant
54:2195:111684:21:19:71:539:253:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for the interpretation of the shading factor (as argued by Wilson (1979)) but also critical
54:2196:111775:19:16:82:539:234:7:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:25Kastl  (2011)  extended  Wilson  model,  which  is  based  on  continuous  and  differentiable  functions,  to
54:2197:111887:16:12:72:540:218:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:more realistic discrete-step functions, showing that in such case only upper and lower bounds on private
54:2198:111991:12:8:72:536:206:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:valuations can be identified, which he does by using the previously methodology on Czech bills auctions.
54:2199:112095:8:16:82:539:198:7:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:26In Canada,  some bidders (dealers) are allowed to observe the bonds of another set of bidders (cos-
54:2200:112196:16:12:72:540:182:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:tumers) when preparing their own bids.  In a private value auction, observing the bid of a costumer only
54:2201:112300:12:12:72:540:170:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:gives information about the competition the dealer faces (and then the probability of winning the auction)
54:2202:112406:12:12:72:540:158:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:but not about the fundamental value of the bond.  In this case the dealer would not revise the bid if this
54:2203:112512:12:12:72:540:146:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:was higher than the observed competing bid. In a common value price auction, however, observing a cos-
54:2204:112614:12:12:72:540:134:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:tumer’s bid induce learning not only of competition but also of the fundamental, leading to a revision of
54:2205:112719:12:12:72:540:122:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:the intended bid also when the bid was higher that the observed competing bid.  Since Canadian auctions
54:2206:112822:12:12:72:540:110:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:are discriminatory, this testable implication is not as straightforward, but they propose a correction. With a
54:2207:112932:12:11:72:540:98:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:similar methodology applied to uniform-price auctions of U.S. Treasury bills, Hortac ̧su, Kastl, and Zhang
54:2208:113038:11:12:72:540:87:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:(2017) estimate that the informational advantage of primary dealers leads them to higher yield bids as a
54:2209:113142:12:0:72:293:75:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:response to a larger ability to bid-shade their bids.
55:2210:113197:0:22:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for thinking about the reaction of bond prices to shocks in volatile times (as highlighted
55:2211:113287:22:22:72:540:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:by Gupta and Lamba (2017)).  The third difference is our modeling of several correlated
55:2212:113374:22:21:72:540:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:shocks, departing heavily from the assumptions of independent realizations across bid-
55:2213:113460:21:22:72:540:643:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ders.  The quality shock, the demand shocks and the signal that all informed investors
55:2214:113546:22:22:72:540:621:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:receive are perfectly correlated, which implies that bid shading only happens for unin-
55:2215:113633:22:21:72:540:599:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:formed investors in response to the possibility of adverse selection, but not because of
55:2216:113721:21:22:72:172:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:competitive forces.
55:2217:113740:22:22:89:539:556:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Closer to our setting, Boyarchenko, Lucca, and Veldkamp (2017) study an auction en-
55:2218:113823:22:21:72:540:534:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:vironment with risk averse investors that are asymmetrically informed about the common
55:2219:113909:21:22:72:540:513:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:value of a bond.  They assume that some investors have both superior information and
55:2220:113993:22:22:72:540:491:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:market power, calibrate the model to U.S. Treasury auctions and show that information
55:2221:114078:22:21:72:540:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sharing across investors increase government revenues, as investors are willing to invest
55:2222:114167:21:22:72:540:448:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:more as they become better informed.  By focusing on the assumption that investors are
55:2223:114253:22:22:72:540:426:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:price-takers we are able to study the effect of asymmetric information on prices instead
55:2224:114341:22:21:72:540:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of on the effect of strategic considerations on prices for both uniform and discriminatory
55:2225:114431:21:53:72:149:383:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:price auctions.
55:2226:114446:53:35:72:188:330:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:8    Conclusion
55:2227:114461:35:21:72:540:295:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We study the determination of sovereign bond yields in primary market auctions.  We
55:2228:114544:21:22:72:540:274:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:view this as an important departure from the literature on sovereign debt that focuses on
55:2229:114633:22:22:72:540:252:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:secondary market prices, because primary market prices are an input to the government’s
55:2230:114720:22:21:72:540:230:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:budget constraint. We start from the perspective that accounting for the evolution of bond
55:2231:114810:21:22:72:540:209:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:prices at issuance necessitates a wide range of shocks, some public, some private, some
55:2232:114897:22:22:72:540:187:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:learnable, some not. Some of these shocks may affect common factors, like the probability
55:2233:114986:22:21:72:540:165:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of default, while others may affect the private valuation of the government’s bonds, like
55:2234:115075:21:22:72:540:144:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:liquidity shocks.  This leads us to develop a rich model of sovereign debt auctions fea-
55:2235:115163:22:22:72:540:122:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:turing shocks to both the default probability of the bond (about which investors can be
55:2236:115250:22:21:72:540:100:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:heterogeneously informed), and a correlated private shock that determines auction par-
55:2237:115336:21:0:72:540:79:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ticipation (about which no investor is informed). This setting provides new insights into
56:2238:115427:0:22:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the impact of different auction protocols on the role and extent of information asymmetry
56:2239:115516:22:22:72:318:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on bond prices in the presence of these shocks.
56:2240:115563:22:21:89:539:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We find that these two protocols behave the same in terms of payoffs and yields when
56:2241:115647:21:22:72:540:643:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:information (or lack of information) is symmetric, albeit with discriminatory-price auc-
56:2242:115735:22:22:72:540:621:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tions offering a lower variation in the yields in response to demand shocks.  These sym-
56:2243:115823:22:21:72:540:599:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:metric cases can be thought of as occurring during tranquil periods when there is no in-
56:2244:115911:21:22:72:540:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:formation to be obtained about the government’s future likelihood of default, or during
56:2245:115998:22:22:72:540:556:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:eventful periods in which this information is publicly and freely available.  Our model
56:2246:116085:22:21:72:540:534:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:also implies that when there is valuable information that can be learned at a cost,  this
56:2247:116174:21:22:72:540:513:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:induces adverse selection that can lead to a wide dispersion in realized auction prices
56:2248:116261:22:22:72:540:491:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and high average yields in discriminatory-price auctions, as uninformed investors are re-
56:2249:116350:22:21:72:540:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:luctant to participate.  While we find that the gains from acquiring information and the
56:2250:116438:21:22:72:540:448:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:adverse selection effects are smaller in uniform price auctions, the conditional variance
56:2251:116527:22:22:72:540:426:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of prices is higher under this protocol.   Finally,  we show that the fraction of informed
56:2252:116617:22:21:72:540:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:investors is never higher in uniform price auctions that in discriminatory auctions, with
56:2253:116706:21:22:72:540:383:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:these last ones also displaying multiple equilibria (one with no investor informed and
56:2254:116792:22:22:72:278:361:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:another with asymmetric information).
56:2255:116829:22:21:89:540:339:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:These results contribute to the wide discussion, dating back at least to Friedman (1960),
56:2256:116918:21:22:72:540:318:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of whether sovereign debt auctions should be conducted with a uniform-price or a price-
56:2257:117005:22:22:72:540:296:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:discriminating protocol.27Our results suggest that the answer to this question is far from
56:2258:117095:22:21:72:540:274:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:straightforward and depends on the nature of shocks, the relative preference of the gov-
56:2259:117183:21:22:72:540:253:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ernment for low average yields or low volatility, the cost of information that determines
56:2260:117272:22:22:72:540:231:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the extent to which investors acquire information and the impact of asymmetric informa-
56:2261:117359:22:22:72:326:209:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tion on the bidding behavior of the uninformed.
56:2262:117406:22:21:89:539:187:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Our model can potentially speak to the kind of data we see in sovereign debt auction,
56:2263:117491:21:22:72:540:166:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:such as the case of Mexican bonds in figure 1.  During crisis periods, when the range of
56:2264:117579:22:19:72:540:144:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:potential default probabilities increase, the model predicts a sharp rise and highly volatile
56:2265:117672:19:15:82:539:125:7:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:27Friedman proposed (pp 64-65) that the U.S. Treasury abandons its previous price-discriminating prac-
56:2266:117774:15:12:72:540:110:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:tice and make all awards at the stopout price instead of at differing prices down through that price. The U.S.
56:2267:117884:12:12:72:540:98:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:Treasury finally adopted this uniform-price protocol for all auctions of 2-year and 5-year notes on Septem-
56:2268:117991:12:12:72:540:86:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:ber 3, 1992.  An excellent summary of this discussion is Chari and Weber (1992).  Earlier discussions about
56:2269:118098:12:0:72:509:74:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:Friedman’s proposal include Goldstein (1962), Friedman (1963), Rieber (1964) and Friedman (1964).
57:2270:118197:0:22:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:interest rates, as those we see during Mexican ”Tequila Crisis” of 1995. When the level of a
57:2271:118289:22:22:72:540:686:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:country’s indebtedness increase there is a substantial pressure for information acquisition
57:2272:118380:22:21:72:540:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and information asymmetry (specially under discriminatory-price auctions), decreasing
57:2273:118465:21:22:72:540:643:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:participation of uninformed investors under the threat of adverse selection and increas-
57:2274:118553:22:22:72:540:621:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ing interest rates even when the quality shock is good.  This reduction in participation
57:2275:118641:22:21:72:540:599:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is also reminiscent of the decline in bids and failed auctions that we commonly observe
57:2276:118728:21:22:72:540:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:during crises.  At the same time, under either symmetric information or symmetric ig-
57:2277:118813:22:22:72:540:556:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:norance when there is little heterogeneity, the additional risk premia associated with de-
57:2278:118903:22:21:72:540:534:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:mand shocks is small. This illustrates how the model can also accommodate the relatively
57:2279:118991:21:22:72:409:513:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:low volatility of the Mexican Cetes interest rates in recent years.
57:2280:119058:22:22:89:539:491:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In a follow-up paper (Cole, Neuhann, and Ordonez (2016)) we examine the implica-
57:2281:119138:22:21:72:540:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tions of discriminatory-price auctions within a two-country setting.  We use the insights
57:2282:119227:21:22:72:540:448:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:developed here to discuss spillovers of information across countries and the role of sec-
57:2283:119316:22:22:72:540:426:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ondary markets.  We show that the sources of complementarities on information acqui-
57:2284:119400:22:21:72:540:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sition inherent to discriminatory-price auctions extend from cross-states to cross-bonds
57:2285:119488:21:22:72:507:383:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and generate spillovers in sovereign spreads even in the absence of other linkages.
57:2286:119571:22:22:89:539:361:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Our model is also applicable to a number of other important cases, including auctions
57:2287:119656:22:21:72:540:339:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of liquidity infusion by central banks, electricity, emission permits, gas, oil, and mineral
57:2288:119748:21:22:72:540:318:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rights.  The key requirement is that the auction involves a sufficiently ”thick” market for
57:2289:119839:22:22:72:540:296:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a homogenous divisible good of uncertain quality so as to make the price-taking assump-
57:2290:119926:22:21:72:540:274:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tion a close approximation to reality.  Our model also provides a potential mechanism to
57:2291:120014:21:22:72:540:253:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:micro-found competitive equilibria for the case of the uniform-price protocol and to break
57:2292:120104:22:0:72:509:231:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the circularity inherent in having prices and quantities determined simultaneously.

65:2582:134165:15:14:71:540:261:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:two consistent prices, and two consistent ̃κ, one in which the short-sale constraint for the
65:2583:134257:14:15:71:539:247:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:informed in the bad state binds and another in which it does not. As explained in the text,

65:2586:134481:14:15:89:539:204:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The fact that for the same supply gap there may be two consistent prices imply that the

65:2591:134950:12:12:72:540:128:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:discontinuous jump down. To see this, replace a common pricePin states(b,1)and(g,ψn)from equation
65:2592:135047:12:12:72:540:116:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:(26) in the auction clearing consistent with no short selling constraint from equation (24), the uninformed
65:2593:135154:12:12:72:540:104:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:investors’ inference that make those two conditions consistent is ̃κ=W−DD(κb−κg)−n1−nκb. The expected
65:2594:135255:12:12:72:540:92:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:probability of default can never be higher than the maximum one feasible, ̃κ≤κb, which only happens if
65:2595:135357:12:0:72:160:80:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f3:F:n≥1−κbκb−κgDW−D.
66:2596:135375:0:15:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to the blue function and keep going down on that function. Consistently, this implies that
66:2597:135465:15:14:72:540:693:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:initially the uninformed become more pessimistic (going up the black function in Panel
66:2598:135551:14:15:72:471:679:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(b), then jumping to the blue function and keep becoming more pessimistic.
66:2599:135625:15:14:89:539:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:It is trivial to see that there is a continuous range in which this jump may occur, so
66:2600:135711:14:15:72:540:650:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:there is an indeterminate number of equilibria characterized by different point at which
66:2601:135799:15:14:72:540:635:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:prices discontinuously change.  All these equilibria are characterized by a single discon-
66:2602:135889:14:15:72:419:621:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tinuous decline in prices, as prices cannot increase in equilibrium.
66:2603:135957:15:14:89:539:606:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The possible nonexistence arises from the constraint that beliefs are consistent with
66:2604:136042:14:14:72:539:592:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f8:B:Bayesian updating. A given ̃κthat is consistent with an equilibrium price for a gapψg−ψb
66:2605:136130:14:15:72:540:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:determines  the  slope  of  the  price  function  that  is  consistent  with  such  inference.   For
66:2606:136230:15:14:72:539:563:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f7:B:instance,  if ̃κis low,  this implies that the price applies for a relatively large mass ofψ
66:2607:136322:14:15:72:540:549:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:points in the good schedule compared to the bad schedule, as discussed in the main text.
66:2608:136410:15:14:72:540:534:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Then, ̃κalso determines the speed at which the gapψg−ψbchanges along the schedules.
66:2609:136493:14:15:72:540:520:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:When the gap is forced to the right of the point in which the two lines cross in Panel (a),
66:2610:136584:15:14:72:278:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:there is no price that clears the auction.
66:2611:136626:14:15:89:539:491:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f16:A:In short, as long as prices for all states are consistent with a gap smaller than(ψg−ψb)∗
66:2612:136715:15:14:71:539:476:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:there is multiplicity.  When for some states prices are forced to be consistent with a gap
66:2613:136805:14:35:71:305:462:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:larger than(ψg−ψb)∗there is non-existence.
66:2614:136847:35:23:71:527:427:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:A.2    Prices when the Short-Sale Constraint Binds on the Uninformed
66:2615:136915:23:15:71:539:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:To  illustrate  how  prices  change  in  a  situation  in  which  the  short-sale  constraint  binds
66:2616:137015:15:14:71:539:389:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for the uninformed investors in the prices that characterizes the symmetric information
66:2617:137102:14:15:71:539:375:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:situation,  we use default probabilities that are closer to each other,  so that those price
66:2618:137194:15:14:71:540:360:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f10:B:schedules are not very far apart.  More precisely, in the example below we useκg= 0.24
66:2619:137280:14:14:71:540:346:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:andκb= 0.29. This change still guarantees that prices in the symmetric information case
66:2620:137367:14:15:71:539:332:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:do not overlap, but now the uninformed wants to bid more at the price corresponding to
66:2621:137453:15:14:71:539:317:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the state[g,ψM]than what they want to bid at the price corresponding to[b,1], which is
66:2622:137539:14:15:72:529:303:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the sufficient condition that breaks condition ii) for perfect replication in proposition 5.
66:2623:137631:15:14:89:539:288:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:When there is no overlap in the price schedule, the binding region is particularly sim-
66:2624:137718:14:15:72:539:274:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ple.   Binding will occur over intervals of the form[ψg,ψM]on theθ=gschedule and
66:2625:137798:15:14:72:540:259:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f3:B:[1,ψb]on theθ=bschedule.  In this case, the total risky bond purchases will be equal
66:2626:137882:14:15:72:540:245:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in this range, and the f.o.c.  ignoring the short-sale constraint hold at the endpoints; i.e.
66:2627:137975:15:14:72:540:230:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:B:BU(g,θg) =BU(b,θb). In contrast to the previous analysis, the f.o.c. does not hold state by
66:2628:138066:14:14:72:540:216:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:state, but the integral of the f.o.c.  over the ranges will equal 0, ass= (g,ψg)is the point
66:2629:138158:14:15:71:539:202:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:at which the short-sale constraint starts binding.  It is easy to see that starting from any
66:2630:138250:15:14:71:539:187:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:B:s= (g,ψg+-)the integral will turn negative, and extending the integral beyond(b,ηb)will
66:2631:138337:14:15:71:539:173:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:turn it positive. Note that, as discussed in section 3.2, when this occurs, an auction equi-
66:2632:138429:15:14:71:539:158:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:librium of the UP model no longer has an associated competitive equilibrium, as this is
66:2633:138516:14:15:71:539:144:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a case of nonnegativity constraints binding for bids in a particular range but not binding
66:2634:138606:15:14:71:245:129:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for total purchases on that range.
66:2635:138640:14:15:89:539:115:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In Figure A.2 we plot the price functions forn= 0.8,0.6and0.4.  As is clear from the
66:2636:138724:15:14:71:539:100:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:figures, the lack of perfect replication has an effect on the price schedules.  Because the
66:2637:138815:14:15:71:539:86:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bids of the uninformed do not adjust to the price over the range that the short-sale binds,
66:2638:138906:15:0:71:539:71:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:it follows that all of the adjustment to match the change in per capita supply must be
67:2639:138994:0:15:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:done by the informed. As they shrink in number, this requires a larger change in the price
67:2640:139084:15:14:72:540:693:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to induce them change their risk exposure and cover those extra bonds. In the high price
67:2641:139172:14:15:72:539:679:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:schedule the uninformed bid a fixed-amount starting from the point(g,ψg)in which the
67:2642:139256:15:14:72:540:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:short-sale constraint binds. The need for extra bonds has to be compensated by informed
67:2643:139343:14:15:72:540:650:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:investors, which depresses prices in equilibrium in the (blue) region[ψg,ψM]. In contrast,
67:2644:139433:15:14:72:540:635:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in the low price schedule, uninformed are bidding more than informed until the point
67:2645:139517:14:15:72:539:621:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f3:B:(b,ψb)at  which  the  short-sale  constraint  stop  binding.   The  extra  demand  inflates  the
67:2646:139613:15:27:72:237:606:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:prices in the (red) region[1,ψb].
